خلاصہ کلام .. صاحبین کے نزدیک بوارہ منازعت کے طریقہ پر ہوگا جس کی تفصیل یہ ہے جو مذکور ہوئی ۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک غلام کو عول اور ضرب کے طریقہ پر تقسیم کیا جائے گا
وعنده يقسم بطريق العول والمضاربة أثلاثا لأن الحق تعلق بالرقبة أصله التركة المستغرقة بالديون فيضرب هذان بالكل وذلك بالنصف ولهذه المسألة نظائر وأضداد ذكرناها في الزيادات ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک غلام عول اور ضرب کے طریقہ پر تقسیم کیا جائے گا تین حصے کر کے اس لئے کہ حق غلام کی گردن سے متعلق ہے اس کی اصل وہ ترکہ ہے جو قرضوں سے گھرا ہوا ہے پس ان دونوں ( ولیان خطاء) کو بحساب کل شریک کیا جائے گا اور ولی عمد کو بحساب نصف شریک کیا جائے گا اور اس مسئلہ کی بہت سی نظیریں اور اضداد ہیں جن کو ہم نے زیادات میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ تشریح امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ تقسیم عول کے طریقہ پر ہوگی یعنی جس طرح عول کے اندر تمام ورثاء گھٹی میں شریک ہوتے ہیں یہاں بھی ان دونوں کو کھٹی میں شریک رکھا جائے گا۔ اور اس کی صورت یہی ہے کہ ان کے حق میں یہی تناسب ہے کہ ولیان خطاء کا حق ولی عمد سے دو گنا ہے اور ولی عمد کا حق ان کے حق سے آدھا ہے لہذا اس نسبت کے بقدر تقسیم کے لئے ۱۳ سے اور ولی عمد کا حق ان کے حق سے آدھا ہے لہذا اس نسبت کے بقدر تقسیم کے لئے ۱۳ سے تقسیم ضروری ہوگی ، لہذا جب ۱۳ سے تقسیم ہوئی تو غلام کے حصے کئے گئے اور ولیان خطاء کو ان میں سے دو اور ولی محمد کو ایک دیا گیا ہے۔ کیونکہ حق کی کمیت میں جو تنا سب ہو گا حق کے بدل کے اندر اس تناسب کو برقرار رکھنا ضروری ہوگا اور وہ یہاں اخلافا تقسیم کئے بغیر نہیں ہوسکتا لہذا غلام کو اعلا تا تقسیم کرنا پڑے گا۔ دور نہ تو ہر فریق کا حق پوری گردن کے ساتھ وابستہ ہے اور یہ طریقہ اختیار کئے بغیر مسئلہ حل نہ ہو گا لہذا سب کو کسی میں شامل کر دیا گیا۔ جیسے اگر زید مرجائے اور اس پر بہت سے قرضے ہوں کہ زید کا ترکہ ان تمام قرضوں کی ادائیگی کے لئے ناکافی ہو تو وہاں بھی یہی عول اور ضرب کا طریقہ کام میں لایا جاتا ہے (تفصیل کے لئے دیکھئے درس سراجی) آگے مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ اس مسئلہ کی کچھ نظائر و اضداد ہیں یعنی کچھ اس کے مثل ہیں اور کچھ اس کے خلاف ہیں جن کو ہم نے زیادات میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کی بھی ایک کتاب کا نام زیادات ہے نیز اس کی ایک ضد ہدایہ قالی ۲۰ پر موجود ہے۔
Commentary: If the slave did not kill both intentionally and by mistake, but rather one intentionally and the other by mistake, then retaliation (qisas) falls. Now what will the master do? There are two possibilities: (1) The master will hand over the slave. (2) He will pay a ransom (fidyah). The ruling of the first will come in the following text, and the ruling of the second is mentioned here, i.e., the master will in this case pay a total of fifteen thousand dirhams, of which five thousand go to the one remaining heir of intentional killing, and ten thousand to the two heirs of accidental killing, because the right of the heirs of accidental killing is ten thousand, so that right is fully obligatory, and in intentional killing since one has forgiven, half the diyah is obligatory, which is five thousand dirhams, so for him five thousand are obligatory, the total becomes fifteen thousand. And if the master chooses to hand over the slave, its ruling is as follows: If the master wants to hand over the slave, what is the procedure? Statements of jurists: (Arabic: And if he hands him over to them in thirds: two-thirds to the two heirs of accidental killing and one-third to the non-pardoning one of the two heirs of intentional killing according to Abu Hanifa. And they (the two companions) said: he hands him over in fourths: three-fourths to the two heirs of accidental killing and one-fourth to the heir of intentional killing. The division according to them is by the method of contention: half is delivered to the heirs of accidental killing without contention, and the contention of the two parties in the other half is equal, so it is halved, hence it is divided into fourths.) Translation: And if the master intends to hand over the slave, then to the heirs, the slave is divided into thirds: two-thirds for both heirs of accidental killing and one-third for the non-pardoning one of the two heirs of intentional killing according to Abu Hanifa. And the two companions said: the master will hand over the slave in fourths: three-fourths for the two heirs of accidental killing and one-fourth for the heir of intentional killing. So according to the two companions, the division is by the method of contention: half is delivered to the two heirs of accidental killing without contention, and in the other half the contention of the two parties is equal, so the last half becomes half-and-half, hence the slave is divided into four parts. Commentary: If the master wants to hand over the slave instead of paying the ransom, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the slave will have three parts: two of them go to the two heirs of accidental killing, and one to the heir of intentional killing who has not pardoned. And according to the two companions, the slave will have four parts: three of them go to the first, and one to the second. The two companions say: Indeed, both parties had a right in the entire slave, each party having the right to take the slave, but what can be done? The slave is only one, so both must be given a share from him. We considered and found that due to the double right of the heirs of accidental killing, half the slave is given to them without contention. Now remaining is the other half; regarding it, contention occurs among these three: the heirs of accidental killing want it because their right remains, so this half should also be given to us; and the heir of intentional killing says: I received nothing, so this half should be mine. Due to this contention, this half is divided in half between them, so now the heirs of accidental killing have three-fourths (3/4) and the heir of intentional killing has one-fourth (1/4). (Top of page 286) Summary: According to the two companions, the division will be by the method of contention, as detailed above. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the slave will be divided by the method of 'awl (proportional reduction) and partnership (mudarabah): (Arabic: And according to him, he divides by the method of 'awl and mudarabah into thirds, because the right is attached to the neck (of the slave); its origin is the estate (tarka) that is overwhelmed by debts; these two (heirs of accidental killing) participate with the whole, and that one (heir of intentional killing) participates with half. This case has many analogues and opposites which we have mentioned in al-Ziyadat.) Translation: And according to Abu Hanifa, the slave is divided by the method of 'awl and mudarabah into three parts, because the right is attached to the neck; its origin is the estate that is overwhelmed by debts; both (heirs of accidental killing) participate as partners in the whole, and the heir of intentional killing participates as a partner in half. And this case has many analogues and opposites which we have mentioned in al-Ziyadat. Commentary: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, this division will be by the method of 'awl, i.e., just as in 'awl all heirs share in the reduction, here also both will be placed in the pool. And its form is that the proportion of their rights is that the right of the heirs of accidental killing is double that of the heir of intentional killing, and the right of the heir of intentional killing is half of theirs. Therefore, for division at this proportion, division into three is necessary. So when divided into three, the slave is made into three parts, and the heirs of accidental killing get two parts, and the heir of intentional killing gets one part, because the proportion in the quantity of right must be maintained in the substitute, and that cannot be done without dividing into three. Therefore, the slave must be divided into three parts. Since each party's right is attached to the whole neck, and without adopting this method the case cannot be resolved, all are included in a common pool. For example, if Zaid dies and has many debts such that his estate is insufficient to pay all debts, then also this method of 'awl and mudarabah is employed. (For details, see Dars Siraji.) The author says: This case has some analogues and opposites, i.e., some similar and some contrary, which we have mentioned in al-Ziyadat. Sahib al-Hidayah also has a book named al-Ziyadat; also there is a contrary (case) in Hidayah Qali on page 20.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the division of a slave who has committed two murders—one intentional and one accidental—when one of the heirs of the intentional victim pardons, and the master chooses to hand over the slave rather than pay diyah. The text first establishes the scenario and the master's options. If the master pays diyah, the total is 15,000 dirhams (5,000 for the non-pardoning heir of intentional killing, 10,000 for the two heirs of accidental killing). If the master hands over the slave, there is a disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). Abu Hanifa divides the slave into three parts: two-thirds to the heirs of accidental killing and one-third to the remaining heir of intentional killing, using the principle of 'awl (proportional reduction) analogous to the distribution of an estate overwhelmed by debts. The two companions divide the slave into four parts: three-fourths to the heirs of accidental killing and one-fourth to the heir of intentional killing, based on the principle of muzara'ah (contention). Their reasoning: half the slave goes uncontested to the heirs of accidental killing due to their double right; the remaining half is contested equally between all three (the two heirs of accidental killing and the one heir of intentional killing), so that half is divided equally, resulting in three-fourths for the accidental heirs and one-fourth for the intentional heir. The commentary elaborates on both methods, noting that Abu Hanifa's approach is analogous to the 'awl in inheritance when debts exceed assets. The passage concludes by mentioning that this case has analogous and contrary cases in al-Ziyadat, a work by the author of al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
عَوْل ('awl): Proportional reduction – when claims exceed assets, shares are reduced proportionally. Here analogized to dividing the slave.
مَنَازَعَة (munaza'ah): Contention or dispute – a principle for resolving competing claims over a single object by splitting the contested portion equally.
مُضَارَبَة (mudarabah): Partnership – here used to describe sharing the slave proportionally, like partners in an estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, what fraction of the slave goes to the heirs of accidental killing when the master hands over the slave?
A) 2/3
B) 3/4
C) 1/2
D) 4/5

Key Takeaway
When a slave is given in diyat and claims are unequal, the Hanafi school offers two valid methods for division: proportional reduction ('awl) and contention (munaza'ah), resulting in different shares.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
6 min
Jointly Owned Slave Kills Both Owners' Relative: Effect of One Pardon
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of one owner's pardon

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the effect of one owner's pardon when a jointly owned slave kills a relative of both owners, and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the disagreement.

Core Idea
Partial pardon by one joint owner invalidates the entire qisas claim according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn require compensation to preserve the other owner's right.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about a slave jointly owned by two men who kills a relative of both. When one owner pardons the slave, what happens to the claims of qisas (retaliation) and diyah (blood money)? The answer differs between Abu Hanifa and his two foremost disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your grasp of how joint rights in qisas interact with partial forgiveness.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the Scenario and Core Issue
Recognise the facts: a slave jointly owned by two men kills a relative who is related to both owners. One owner pardons the slave. The dispute centres on whether the pardon extinguishes all claims (qisas/diyah) or only the pardoning owner's share.
The text clarifies that 'mawla' here means a close relative, not a master.
2
2. State Abu Hanifa's Ruling and Rationale
According to Abu Hanifa (and Muhammad in some narrations), the entire claim (qisas and diyah) becomes invalid. The slave is not subject to any further claim from either owner. The likely rationale: qisas is a single, indivisible right held jointly by the victims' heirs; partial pardon extinguishes the entire right.
This position treats the right of qisas as a unified whole.
3
3. State the Sahibayn's Ruling and Rationale
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (in the main narration), the pardoning owner must compensate the other owner. He either pays half of his share of the slave's value to the other owner, or he ransoms with a quarter of the diyah (i.e., half the diyah for his share). The rationale: only the pardoning owner's share is forfeited; the other owner retains his share of the right.
This view treats qisas as a divisible right where each co-heir has an independent portion.
4
4. Note Variant Narrations and Muhammad's Position
The text records that in some copies, Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa. In the Ziyadat, a similar case is mentioned where a slave kills his master who has two sons; one son pardons. There, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold the claim invalid, while Abu Yusuf requires compensation. This shows the transmission of multiple riwayat within the Hanafi school.
Variant narrations indicate that the issue was not settled unanimously among the early Hanafis.
5
5. Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: Under Abu Hanifa, the pardoning owner loses his share in the slave (since the slave is no longer subject to any claim, but ownership continues? Actually the slave remains owned, but the right to claim qisas is lost; the owners retain the slave but cannot demand anything from each other). Under the Sahibayn, the non-pardoning owner receives compensation (either part of the slave's value or diyah). This difference affects how the joint owners settle the matter after the pardon.
The mufta bihi (relied upon opinion) is not specified in the passage, but later Hanafi works may prefer one view.

Source Text

ایک غلام دو آدمیوں کے درمیان مشترک ہے اس غلام نے ان دونوں کے قریب کو قتل کر دیا ان دونوں میں سے ایک نے معاف کر دیا تو قصاص باطل ہے
قال وإذا كان عبد بين رجلين فقتل مولى لهما أى قريبا لهما فعفا أحدهما بطل الجميع عند أبي حنيفة وقالا يدفع الذي عفا نصف نصيبه إلى الآخر أو يفديه بربع الدية وذكر في بعض النسخ قتل وليا لهما والمراد القريب أيضا وذكر في بعض النسخ قول محمد مع أبي حنيفة وذكر في الزيادات عبد قتل مولاه وله ابنان فعفا أحد الابنين بطل ذلك كله عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد وعند أبي يوسف الجواب فيه كالجواب في مسألة الكتاب ولم يذكر اختلاف الرواية
A slave is shared between two men; this slave killed a relative of both; one of them pardoned, so qisas is invalid. (Arabic: He said: If there is a slave between two men and he kills a mawla of both, i.e., a relative of both, and one of them pardons, then the whole is invalid according to Abu Hanifa. And they (the two companions) said: the one who pardons pays half of his share to the other, or he may ransom it with a quarter of the diyah. It is mentioned in some copies: he killed a wali of both, and the intended meaning is also a relative. And it is mentioned in some copies: the statement of Muhammad is with Abu Hanifa. And it is mentioned in al-Ziyadat: a slave killed his mawla, and he (the mawla) had two sons; one of the sons pardoned; all of that is invalid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. According to Abu Yusuf, the answer in it is like the answer in the case of the book (the main case), and he did not mention the difference in narration.)
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage introduces a separate case: a slave jointly owned by two men kills a relative (mawla or wali) of both owners. If one of the owners pardons the slave, there is disagreement. According to Abu Hanifa, the entire claim (qisas or diyah) is invalidated (batala al-jami'). According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), the pardoning owner must either pay half of his share of the slave to the other owner or ransom with a quarter of the diyah. The text notes variant narrations: some versions have Muhammad agreeing with Abu Hanifa, and in al-Ziyadat a similar case is mentioned where a slave kills his master, and the master has two sons; one son pardons; according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad the whole is invalid, while Abu Yusuf treats it like the main case in the book (the case from the previous lesson). This shows an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, with varying narrations.

Key Terms
مَوْلَى (mawla): In this context, a close relative (qarib). The text clarifies that it means a relative.
وَلِيّ (wali): In some narrations, used synonymously with mawla meaning a relative; also heir of the victim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the main narration of Sahibayn, what must the pardoning owner do if a jointly owned slave kills a relative of both?
A) He must pay the full diyah to the other owner
B) He must pay half his share of the slave to the other owner or pay one-fourth of the diyah
C) He must hand over the slave entirely to the other owner
D) No compensation is required

Key Takeaway
The pardon of one joint owner of a slave who killed a relative of both invalidates the entire qisas claim according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn require the pardoning owner to compensate the other.

The Slave's Division: Abu Hanifa's 'Awl and Mudaraba vs. Sahibayn's Muwara'ah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dividing a slave with multiple diyat claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's method of dividing a slave among diyat claimants using 'awl and mudaraba, explain the analogical reasoning (qiyas) to an insolvent estate, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf with the Sahibayn's position.

Core Idea
When a slave's value is insufficient for multiple diyat claims, Abu Hanifa divides proportionally like an insolvent estate.

The Hidayah presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute about how to divide a slave who has been subject to two types of homicide: intentional ('amd) and accidental (khata'). The slave's value must satisfy the diyat claims of the guardians. Imam Abu Hanifa applies the principles of 'awl (proportional reduction) and mudaraba (sharing), drawing an analogy to an estate overwhelmed by debts. The Sahibayn differ, but their exact method is only referenced as 'muwara'ah minaza'at'. We will unpack Abu Hanifa's reasoning and the practical difference between the two views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting claims
State the parties: two guardians for two accidental killings (each claiming full diyat) and one guardian for intentional killing (claiming half diyat). Note the total claims exceed the slave's value.
The exact numbers are not critical; what matters is the proportional strength of claims.
2
State Abu Hanifa's method
He divides the slave by 'awl and mudaraba, meaning the claimants share proportionally. Each khata' guardian gets a full share; the 'amd guardian gets half a share. This yields a 2:2:1 ratio.
The Hidayah mentions dividing into 13 parts, but the principle is proportional sharing, not the exact number.
3
Trace the legal analogy (qiyas)
Abu Hanifa analogizes to an insolvent estate (tarika mustaghraqa bi-duyun). In both cases, multiple claimants compete for a limited asset; all share proportionally. The 'illah is that the right attaches to the entire asset (raqaba).
This is a clear qiyas jaliy: the original case (asl) is the estate with debts, the new case (far') is the slave with diyat claims, and the 'illah is the insufficiency of the asset to cover all claims.
4
Compare with Sahibayn
The Sahibayn have a different method (muwara'ah minaza'at), but the text does not detail it. The thamarah al-khilaf is the distribution outcome.
The passage only mentions that Sahibayn's method was described earlier.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Abu Hanifa's method requires physical division of the slave into shares (parts), each claimant taking a portion. The Sahibayn likely avoid such division by having the slave work or by a different valuation process.
Understanding this difference clarifies why the method matters in practice.

خلاصہ کلام .. صاحبین کے نزدیک بوارہ منازعت [؟] کے طریقہ پر ہوگا جس کی تفصیل یہ ہے جو مذکور ہوئی ۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک غلام کو عول اور ضرب کے طریقہ پر تقسیم کیا جائے گا وعنده يقسم بطريق العول والمضاربة أثلاثا لأن الحق تعلق بالرقبة أصله التركة المستغرقة بالديون فيضرب هذان بالكل وذلك بالنصف ولهذه المسألة نظائر وأضداد ذكرناها في الزيادات ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک غلام عول اور ضرب کے طریقہ پر تقسیم کیا جائے گا تین حصے کر کے اس لئے کہ حق غلام کی گردن سے متعلق ہے اس کی اصل وہ ترکہ ہے جو قرضوں سے گھرا ہوا ہے پس ان دونوں ( ولیان خطاء) کو بحساب کل شریک کیا جائے گا اور ولی عمد کو بحساب نصف شریک کیا جائے گا اور اس مسئلہ کی بہت سی نظیریں اور اضداد ہیں جن کو ہم نے زیادات میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ تشریح امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ تقسیم عول کے طریقہ پر ہوگی یعنی جس طرح عول کے اندر تمام ورثاء گھٹی میں شریک ہوتے ہیں یہاں بھی ان دونوں کو کھٹی میں شریک رکھا جائے گا۔ اور اس کی صورت یہی ہے کہ ان کے حق میں یہی تناسب ہے کہ ولیان خطاء کا حق ولی عمد سے دو گنا ہے اور ولی عمد کا حق ان کے حق سے آدھا ہے لہذا اس نسبت کے بقدر تقسیم کے لئے ۱۳ سے اور ولی عمد کا حق ان کے حق سے آدھا ہے لہذا اس نسبت کے بقدر تقسیم کے لئے ۱۳ سے تقسیم ضروری ہوگی ، لہذا جب ۱۳ سے تقسیم ہوئی تو غلام کے حصے کئے گئے اور ولیان خطاء کو ان میں سے دو اور ولی محمد کو ایک دیا گیا ہے۔ کیونکہ حق کی کمیت میں جو تنا سب ہو گا حق کے بدل کے اندر اس تناسب کو برقرار رکھنا ضروری ہوگا اور وہ یہاں اخلافا تقسیم کئے بغیر نہیں ہوسکتا لہذا غلام کو اعلا تا تقسیم کرنا پڑے گا۔ دور نہ تو ہر فریق کا حق پوری گردن کے ساتھ وابستہ ہے اور یہ طریقہ اختیار کئے بغیر مسئلہ حل نہ ہو گا لہذا سب کو کسی میں شامل کر دیا گیا۔ جیسے اگر زید مرجائے اور اس پر بہت سے قرضے ہوں کہ زید کا ترکہ ان تمام قرضوں کی ادائیگی کے لئے ناکافی ہو تو وہاں بھی یہی عول اور ضرب کا طریقہ کام میں لایا جاتا ہے (تفصیل کے لئے دیکھئے درس سراجی) آگے مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ اس مسئلہ کی کچھ نظائر و اضداد ہیں یعنی کچھ اس کے مثل ہیں اور کچھ اس کے خلاف ہیں جن کو ہم نے زیادات میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کی بھی ایک کتاب کا نام زیادات ہے نیز اس کی ایک ضد ہدایہ قالی ۲۰ پر موجود ہے۔
Summary of speech: According to the two companions (Sahibayn), it will be by the method of muwara'ah minaza'at [؟], the detail of which is what has been mentioned. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the slave will be divided by the method of 'awl and mudaraba: 'And with him, he divides it by the method of 'awl and mudaraba into three parts, because the right is attached to the neck; its origin is the estate that is overwhelmed by debts; so these two (the two guardians of khata') participate with the whole, and that one (the guardian of 'amd) with the half. And this issue has parallels and opposites that we have mentioned in al-Ziyadat.' Translation: And according to Abu Hanifa, the slave will be divided by the method of 'awl and mudaraba into three parts, because the right is attached to the slave's neck; its origin is the estate that is overwhelmed by debts; so these two (the two guardians of khata') are included with the full (share), and the guardian of 'amd with half. And this issue has many parallels and opposites that we have mentioned in al-Ziyadat. Explanation: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, this division will be by the method of 'awl, i.e., just as in 'awl all heirs share in the pool, here too both are included in the pool. And its form is that the proportion of their rights is such that the right of the two guardians of khata' is twice that of the guardian of 'amd, and the right of the guardian of 'amd is half of theirs. Therefore, for division according to this proportion, division by 13 is necessary. So when divided by 13, the slave's shares were made, and the two guardians of khata' were given two of them and the guardian of 'amd was given one. Because the proportion that exists in the quantity of the right must be maintained in the substitute of the right, and it cannot happen without dividing into parts. Therefore, the slave must be divided into parts. Otherwise, each party's right is attached to the whole neck, and this matter cannot be resolved without adopting this method. So all are included in one. For example, if Zayd dies and he has many debts such that Zayd's estate is insufficient to pay all debts, then there too the same method of 'awl and mudaraba is employed (for details, see Dars Siraji). The author says further: This issue has some parallels and opposites, i.e., some are like it and some are contrary to it, which we have mentioned in al-Ziyadat. The author of Hidayah also has a book named al-Ziyadat; also its opposite exists on page 20 of Hidayah Qali.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the division of a slave who has been subject to multiple diyat claims for both 'amd (intentional homicide) and khata' (accidental homicide). The slave's entire value is to be divided between the guardians of the two types of homicide. Imam Abu Hanifa (RA) holds that the division should follow the method of 'awl (proportional reduction) and mudaraba (sharing), treating the slave as an estate overwhelmed by debts. He analogizes the situation to an insolvent estate where creditors share proportionally. According to Abu Hanifa, the two guardians of khata' (each claiming full diyat for accidental killing) are to be treated as having full shares, while the guardian of 'amd (claiming diyat for intentional killing) gets half a share, resulting in a total of 2.5 shares, which simplifies to a ratio of 2:2:1 (for the two khata' guardians and one 'amd guardian). The author explains that this requires dividing the slave into 13 parts (since 2+2+1=5, but then multiplied? Actually the text says divide by 13, which seems odd; possibly it is a different proportion or a typo. The commentary then describes the division: the two khata' guardians get two parts each, and the 'amd guardian gets one part, making total 5 parts? The number 13 is unclear. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) apparently have a different method (buwarah minaza'at [؟]), which is not elaborated here but referred to as having been mentioned earlier. The passage concludes by noting that this issue has parallels and opposites in al-Ziyadat, a separate work by the author of al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
عول ('awl): Proportional reduction of shares in inheritance when the total of prescribed shares exceeds the estate; applied here to division of a slave's value.
مضاربة (mudaraba): Sharing or partnership; here used to mean proportional participation of claimants.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, how is the slave to be divided between the guardians of 'amd and khata'?
A) Equally among all guardians
B) By 'awl and mudaraba proportionally based on the strength of claims
C) By lottery
D) The slave is set free and no division occurs

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa divides a slave subject to multiple diyat claims by proportional 'awl and mudaraba, analogizing to an insolvent estate, with the Sahibayn holding a different method that is not detailed in this passage.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
8 min
Pardon by One Owner of a Shared Slave Who Killed Their Relatives
Intra-Hanafi dispute on partial pardon in shared slave killing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the effect of a co-owner's pardon and explain the legal reasoning (shuyu') behind Abu Hanifa's ruling.

Core Idea
A partial pardon voids all claims because the common right becomes ambiguous.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a slave co-owned by two persons who kills a relative of each owner. When one owner pardons the slave, does the other owner lose his right to qisas or diyah? Imam Abu Hanifa holds that all claims are nullified, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) offer a different remedy. Understanding the concept of shuyu' (commonness of right) is key to grasping the legal reasoning behind these positions.

Guided Path
1
State the case and the issue
Identify the scenario: a slave co-owned by two persons kills a relative of each owner. One owner pardons the slave. The issue is the effect on the other owner's right to qisas or diyah.
2
Identify the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the pardon nullifies all claims for both owners—no qisas and no diyah. Understand the reasoning: the right of qisas was common (shuyu') and after partial pardon, the remaining right becomes ambiguous as to which part of the slave it attaches to.
3
Identify the opposing position (Sahibayn)
Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (in some narrations) hold that the other owner does not lose all rights. The pardoning owner must either give half his share in the slave to the other owner or pay a quarter of the diyah. This converts the qisas right into a property claim.
Note: In some copies, Muhammad's statement is with Abu Hanifa; the more famous narration pairs Muhammad with Abu Yusuf.
4
Follow the reasoning (shuyu' and ambiguity)
Abu Hanifa's argument is based on the commonness (shuyu') of the qisas right. Prior to pardon, the right was shared like ownership. After partial pardon, the remaining right is ambiguous: it is unclear which part of the slave it corresponds to, so the entire claim fails. The Sahibayn do not accept this conclusion; they see the remaining right as convertible into property.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the other owner gets nothing; under Sahibayn, he receives additional ownership or payment. The text indicates the view of Muhammad with Abu Yusuf is more famous (ashhar), suggesting a preference in later fatwa.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, and both positions are within the school's range of valid rulings.

بدل ہے جیسے اس میں یہ احتمال ہے کہ شاید یہ اس کے نصف کا بدل ہو جو بکر کا ہے ایسے ہی اس میں یہ
A slave is shared between two men; this slave killed a relative of both; one of them pardoned; so qisas is void. He said: And when a slave is between two men, and he kills a mawla of theirs, i.e., a relative of theirs, and one of them pardons, then all is void according to Abu Hanifa. And they (the two companions) said: The one who pardons gives half of his share to the other or ransoms it with a quarter of the diyah. And it is mentioned in some copies: 'he killed a wali of theirs' and the meaning is also a relative. And in some copies, the statement of Muhammad is with Abu Hanifa. And it is mentioned in al-Ziyadat: A slave killed his master, and he had two sons; one of the sons pardoned; then all that is void according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and according to Abu Yusuf, the answer is the same as the answer in the issue of the book. And he did not mention the difference of narration. Translation: Imam Muhammad said: And when a slave is between two men, and this slave kills a relative of both, then when one of them pardons, all is void (qisas and property) according to Abu Hanifa. And the two companions said: The one who pardoned gives half of his share to the other or ransoms it with a quarter of the diyah. And in some copies of al-Jami' al-Saghir, it is mentioned: qatala waliyyan lahuma, and that also means relative. And in some copies, the statement of Muhammad is mentioned with Abu Hanifa. And in al-Ziyadat, it is mentioned: A slave killed his master, and he had two sons; so when one of the two sons pardoned the killing, then all this is void according to Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad. And according to Abu Yusuf, the answer is the same as the answer in the issue of the book. And Imam Muhammad, when presenting this issue in al-Ziyadat and al-Jami' al-Saghir, did not mention the difference of narration. Explanation: In this issue, there are five things to understand. 1. In the copies of al-Jami' al-Saghir, there is a difference: in some it is 'qatala mawla lahuma' and in some 'qatala waliyyan lahuma'; in any case, the meaning is the same. 2. In some copies of al-Jami' al-Saghir, the statement of Imam Muhammad is reported with Imam Abu Hanifa, i.e., they have one statement; and here Muhammad's statement is reported with Imam Abu Yusuf, and this is more famous. 3. The author presented a sub-case from al-Ziyadat: A slave killed his master, and the murdered master had two sons who had the right to qisas; but one of them pardoned the slave. So according to both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), everything is void, i.e., neither qisas remains nor property. And according to Imam Abu Yusuf, here too the same ruling applies as in the issue of al-Jami' al-Saghir, where the position of the two companions was stated, and the difference of narration is not mentioned; rather it is clearly written that Abu Yusuf says this and the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) say that. 4. Explanation of the issue: Zayd and Bakr have a shared slave; the slave commits the mischief that he killed Zayd's father and also killed Bakr's father; so both had the right of qisas. But Zayd pardons the slave. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, Bakr's right is also void, i.e., now neither Zayd nor Bakr can take qisas nor property. And the madhhab of the two companions is that in the mentioned case, when the owner of half the slave is, for example, Zayd, and Bakr owns the other half, then Bakr will become the owner of Zayd's half as well, i.e., if Zayd agrees, then the ownership of the slave will be in quarters: Bakr's 3/4 and Zayd's 1/4; or Zayd pays a ransom of half of his half, i.e., 1/4 of the diyah. 5. Here the author did not present a proof for the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions. But a summary of Imam's proof is that before the pardon, the right of both was established as qisas, which had shuyu' (commonness) like the commonness in ownership. Now when Zayd pardoned, his share falls. And according to the prior state, Bakr's right changes to property, and Bakr's share is half. But now there is a doubt: the property that will be given to Bakr is the substitute for which half? There is a possibility that it is the substitute for his own half, and similarly...
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a slave co-owned by two persons who kills a relative of each owner. The issue arises when one owner pardons the slave, potentially affecting the other owner's right to qisas or diyah. According to Imam Abu Hanifa (RA), the pardon by one owner nullifies all claims—both qisas and financial compensation—for both owners. The reasoning is that the right of qisas was established as a common right (shuyu') attached to the entire slave; when one owner pardons, his portion of the right falls, and the remaining right becomes ambiguous as to which part of the slave it attaches to, leading to the entire claim being void. The Sahibayn (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani) differ: they hold that the pardoning owner must either transfer half of his share in the slave to the other owner (thus making the other owner own three-quarters and the pardoning owner one-quarter) or ransom it by paying a quarter of the full diyah. In essence, the other owner's right is not void but is converted into a property claim. The passage also notes a variant case from al-Ziyadat: a slave owned by a single master kills the master, leaving two sons. If one son pardons, Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad say all claims are void, while Abu Yusuf applies the same ruling as in the co-owned slave case. The commentary clarifies the five points: textual variants in al-Jami' al-Saghir, the position of Imam Muhammad (sometimes with Abu Hanifa, sometimes with Abu Yusuf), the separate case from al-Ziyadat, a detailed explanation using the example of Zayd and Bakr, and the absence of explicit dalil in the text. The author then provides a summary of Imam Abu Hanifa's reasoning based on shuyu' and ambiguity.

Key Terms
عرش (arsh): Compensation for injury; here used in context of diyah for killing.
شىوع (shuyu'): Commonness or shared nature of a right; here the right of qisas is shared between the two owners in proportion to their ownership of the slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the more famous (ashhar) narration within this passage, with whom is Imam Muhammad's position aligned?
A) Abu Hanifa
B) Abu Yusuf
C) Alone, different from both
D) Not mentioned

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa voids all claims after a partial pardon due to shuyu' and ambiguity, while the Sahibayn convert the remaining right into a property claim.

Diyat — Blood Money
advanced
10 min
Effect of One Co-Owner's Pardon in Joint Ownership of a Slave
Intra-Hanafi dispute on pardon by one co-owner

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the effect of one co-owner’s pardon of a jointly owned slave, explain the reasoning behind each, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When one co-owner pardons a jointly owned slave, the other’s right does not automatically lapse—the Sahibayn preserve it as a claim for compensation, while Abu Hanifah voids everything due to uncertainty.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute in the law of diyat. The scenario involves a slave jointly owned by two persons who kills both owners' fathers. When one owner pardons the slave, the question arises: does the other owner lose his right entirely, or does it convert into a financial claim? Imam Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) offer conflicting answers, each grounded in careful reasoning about joint rights (shuyu') and the impossibility of a master being indebted to his own slave. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to analyze the interaction of joint rights and compensation in Islamic criminal law.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Identify the parties and the act: a slave is jointly owned by Zayd and Bakr. The slave kills both Zayd's father and Bakr's father. Both have the right to qisas. Zayd pardons the slave.
2
Identify the two positions
State Abu Hanifah's view: the pardon makes everything void (no qisas, no wealth). State the Sahibayn's view: the pardoning owner must give half of his share of the slave to the other owner or pay 1/4 of the diyah.
3
Follow the reasoning of Abu Hanifah
Understand his argument: before pardon, the right to qisas was joint (shuyu'). When Zayd pardoned, his share dropped. Bakr's share converted to wealth, but due to the jointness, there is uncertainty (shakk) whether the wealth corresponds to Bakr's half or the pardoned half. Therefore, no wealth can be obligated.
Doubt prevents obligation of financial rights.
4
Follow the reasoning of the Sahibayn
Understand their argument: the right was also joint. When one pardoned, the other's half turned into wealth but remained joint in the whole. Half of that half (i.e., one-fourth of the whole) lies in the non-pardoning owner's own share (drops because master cannot owe his slave). The other half lies in the pardoning owner's share (remains). Hence, the pardoning owner must give half his share (equivalent to one-fourth of the whole slave) or ransom with 1/4 of the diyah.
This preserves the other owner's right without the master-owed-to-slave problem.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifah, the non-pardoning owner loses all rights. Under the Sahibayn, he receives compensation. The relied-upon position for fatwa is the Sahibayn's view, as it avoids complete lapse of rights and is preferred by later Hanafi jurists.
The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's position.

امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل
لأبي يوسف أن حق القصاص ثبت فى العبد على سبيل الشيوع لأن ملك المولى لا يمنع استحقاق القصاص له فإذا عفا أحدهما انقلب نصيب الآخر وهو النصف مالا غير أنه شائع في الكل فيكون نصفه في نصيبه والنصف في نصيب صاحبه فما يكون فى نصيبه سقط ضرورة أن المولى لا يستوجب على عبده مالا وما كان فى نصيب صاحبه بقى ونصف النصف هو الربع فلهذا يقال ادفع نصف نصيبك أو افتده بربع الدية
ترجمہ 14 ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ غلام میں حق قصاص شیوع کے طریقہ پر ثابت ہوا ہے اس لئے کہ آقا کی ملکیت آقا کے لئے قصاص کے استحقاق کو نہیں روکتی پس جب ان دونوں میں سے ایک نے معاف کر دیا تو دوسرے کا حصہ مال سے بدل گیا۔ اور وہ (نصیب آخر ) نصف ہے مگر وہ نصف ( بھی ) کل میں پھیلا ہوا ہے تو اس کا نصف (نصف کا نصف ) اس کے حصہ میں ہو گا ( بکر کے) اور نصف اس کے ساتھی کے حصہ میں ( زید کے جو معاف کرنے والا ہے ) پس جو نصف اس کے ( بکر کے ) حصہ میں پڑے گا وہ تو ساقط ہو جائے گا اس بات کی ضرورت کی وجہ سے کہ آقا اپنے غلام پر مال کا (دین کا مستحق نہیں ہوتا اور جو نصف اس کے ساتھی کے حصہ میں پڑے گاوہ باقی رہے گا اور نصف کا نصف وہ ربع ہے اس وجہ سے معاف کرنے والے سے کہا جائے گا کہ اپنے حصہ کا نصف غلام دیدے یا چوتھائی دیت کے ساتھ اس کا فدیہ ادا کر دے۔ تشریح یہ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل ہے اس مسئلہ میں جو زیادات میں مذکور ہے اور یہی جامع صغیر کی روایت کے مطابق صاحبین کی دلیل ہے۔ حاصل دلیل یہ ہے کہ آقا اس غلام کے اب دو ہیں ایک زید اور دوسرا بکر کیونکہ یہ دونوں مقتول کے بیٹے ہیں تو قصاص لینے کا حق دونوں کو حاصل ہے لیکن یہ حق قصاص بطریق ۔ شیوع ہے اور شیوع اور ملک آقا دونوں اس بات کو ممنوع نہیں قرار دیتے کہ حق آقا بن کر قصاص واجب ہو، بہر حال شیوع کے طریقہ پر حق قصاص دونوں کے لئے ثابت ہے پھر زید نے اس غلام کو معاف کر دیا تو اب قصاص تو بالکلیہ ساقط ہو گیا اور اب بکر کا حق قصاص مال سے بدل گیا اور بکر کا حق فقط نصف ہے مگر گل میں شائع ہے تو اب بدالبہ بکر کا نصف حق تو اپنے حصہ میں ہوگا اور نصف زید کے کیونکہ شیوع کا یہی تقاضہ ہے تو جو نصف حق بکر کے حصہ میں ہوگا۔ اس کو تو ساقط کرنا پڑیگا یعنی اس کا ضمان واجب نہیں ہو گا ورنہ اس کا مطلب یہ ہو جائے گا کہ آقا ( بکر) اپنے غلام پر اپنے دین و قرض کا مستحق ہو گیا حالانکہ یہ باطل ہے۔ البتہ دوسرا نصف وہ بیچا جو زید کے حصہ میں پڑتا ہے اس میں یہ خرابی لازم نہیں آتی اور وہ نصف جو زید کے حصہ میں پڑتا ہے چونکہ وہ یہاں نصف کا نصف ہے اور نصف کا نصف ربع ہوتا ہے لہذا اب زید سے کہا جائے گا کہ اپنے حصہ کا نصف بکر کو دیدے تو بکر پہلے
Book of Diyat. Ashraf al-Bidayah Sharh Urdu Hidayah Volume 15. Translation: Umm Muhammad said: And when there is a slave between two persons, and that slave killed their close relatives, then one of the two pardoned, then everything becomes void (qisas and wealth) according to Abu Hanifah. And the Sahibayn said: The one who pardoned will give half of his share to the other or ransom it with one-fourth of the blood money. And in some copies of Jami' al-Saghir it is mentioned: 'he killed their two guardians' and by that also close relatives are meant. And in some copies Muhammad's statement is mentioned with Abu Hanifah. And in Ziyadat it is mentioned that a slave killed his master and he had two sons, then one of the two sons pardoned the killing, then it became entirely void according to Abu Hanifah and Imam Muhammad. And according to Abu Yusuf, the same answer applies as in the issue of this book. And Imam Muhammad in Ziyadat and Jami' al-Saghir did not mention the difference of narration while stating this issue. Explanation: In this issue there are five things to understand. 1. In copies of Jami' al-Saghir, there is difference: in some it is 'faqatala mawla lahumaa' and in some 'qatala waliyya lahumaa' – in any case the meaning of both is one. 2. In some copies of Jami' al-Saghir, Imam Muhammad's statement is told with Imam Abu Hanifah, i.e., both have one statement, and here Muhammad's statement is told with Imam Abu Yusuf, and this is more famous. 3. The author presented a detail from Ziyadat: a slave killed his master and that killed master had two sons who had the right to take qisas, but one of them pardoned the slave. Then according to the two (Abu Hanifah and Muhammad) everything became void, i.e., neither qisas nor wealth remained, and according to Imam Abu Yusuf, here also the same ruling will apply as in the issue of Jami' al-Saghir. The position of the Sahibayn is stated and the difference of narration is not mentioned, rather it is clearly written that Abu Yusuf says this and the two say that. Clarification of the issue: Zayd and Bakr have a jointly owned slave. The slave committed the crime of killing Zayd's father and also Bakr's father. So both had the right of qisas. But Zayd pardoned the slave. Then according to Imam Abu Hanifah, Bakr's right also became void, i.e., now neither can take qisas nor wealth, neither Zayd nor Bakr. And the madhhab of the Sahibayn is that in the mentioned scenario, when half of the slave is owned by, e.g., Zayd and half by Bakr, then Zayd's half also becomes owned by Bakr, i.e., if Zayd agrees, then both's ownership in the slave becomes in fourths, i.e., Bakr's 3/4 and Zayd's 1/4; or Zayd gives the ransom of half of his half, i.e., pays 1/4 of the blood money. 5. Here the author did not state the proof for the positions of Imam Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn. But the summary of Imam Abu Hanifah's proof is that before pardon, both's right had become established as qisas which was joint (shuyu'), like jointness in ownership. Now when Zayd pardoned, his share dropped. And according to the earlier, Bakr's right converted to wealth, and Bakr's share is half, but now doubt arose as to which half the wealth given to Bakr is the substitute for – there is probability that it is the substitute for the half that is Bakr's, and similarly probability that it is for the other half that has already been pardoned. In any case, this doubt arose, and wealth does not become obligatory due to doubt and uncertainty. Imam Abu Yusuf's proof: The text of Abu Yusuf: 'Because the right of qisas was established in the slave on the basis of jointness (al-shuyu'), because the ownership of the master does not prevent the entitlement of qisas for him. So when one of them pardoned, the share of the other, which is half, turned into wealth, but it is joint in the whole, so half of it is in his share and half in the share of his companion. So what is in his share drops necessarily because the master is not entitled to wealth from his slave, and what is in the share of his companion remains, and half of half is one-fourth. Therefore it is said: give half of your share or ransom it with one-fourth of the blood money.' Translation 14: The proof of Abu Yusuf is that the right of qisas was established in the slave on the basis of jointness, because the ownership of the master does not prevent the entitlement of qisas for him. So when one of them pardoned, the other's share turned into wealth, and it (the other share) is half, but that half is also spread in the whole, so half of it (half of half) will be in his share (Bakr's) and half in the share of his companion (Zayd's, who pardoned). So the half that falls in his (Bakr's) share will drop because of the necessity that the master is not entitled to wealth from his slave, and the half that falls in his companion's share will remain, and half of half is one-fourth. For this reason, the one who pardoned will be told: give half of your share of the slave or ransom it with one-fourth of the blood money. Explanation: This is the proof of Imam Abu Yusuf in this issue which is mentioned in Ziyadat, and this is the proof of the Sahibayn according to the narration of Jami' al-Saghir. The summary of the proof is that there are now two masters of this slave: one Zayd and the other Bakr, because both are sons of the killed, so both have the right to take qisas. But this right of qisas is on the basis of jointness (shuyu'), and jointness and the ownership of the master do not prevent that the right of the master becomes established as qisas. In any case, the right of qisas is established for both on the basis of jointness. Then Zayd pardoned the slave. Now qisas dropped entirely. And now Bakr's right of qisas turned into wealth. And Bakr's right is only half, but is joint in the whole. So this substitute for Bakr's half right will be in his own share (half of it) and half in Zayd's share because jointness requires this. So the half of the right that is in Bakr's share will have to be dropped, i.e., its guarantee is not obligatory, otherwise it would mean that the master (Bakr) becomes entitled to his own slave's wealth, which is invalid. However, the other half, i.e., the portion that falls in Zayd's share, this defect does not necessarily apply, and that half that falls in Zayd's share is half of half, and half of half is one-fourth. Therefore Zayd will be told to give half of his share to Bakr, so that Bakr first
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is a commentary on a ruling from the chapter of Diyat (blood money). The issue is a jointly owned slave who kills two people—specifically the fathers of the two co-owners. The central dispute is between Imam Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad). The passage first states the ruling: according to Abu Hanifah, if one co-owner pardons the slave, everything (qisas and financial compensation) is void for both. According to the Sahibayn, the pardoning owner must give half of his share of the slave to the other owner, or ransom it with one-fourth of the blood money. The commentary then discusses variations in the manuscripts of Jami' al-Saghir and Ziyadat, noting differences in wording and attribution of Muhammad's position. It clarifies that the issue involves a slave belonging to Zayd and Bakr who kills both of their fathers. The explanation of Abu Hanifah's reasoning is that before pardon, the right to qisas was joint (shuyu'), similar to joint ownership. When one pardons, his share drops, and the other's share converts to wealth, but uncertainty arises: the wealth cannot be assigned to a specific half of the right (since one half belongs to the pardoning owner and the other to the non-pardoning). Due to this doubt, no wealth becomes obligatory. Abu Yusuf's proof, quoted in Arabic, argues that the right of qisas was established on the basis of jointness because the master's ownership does not preclude qisas entitlement. When one pardons, the other's share (half) turns into wealth but remains joint in the whole. Thus half of that half is in the non-pardoning owner's own share and therefore cannot be claimed from the slave (since a master cannot be owed by his own slave), so it drops. The other half lies in the pardoning owner's share and remains, so the pardoning owner must hand over half of his share (which equals one-fourth of the entire slave) or pay one-fourth of the blood money as ransom. This dispute is intra-Hanafi, with both positions having textual support. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the late Hanafi school is the Sahibayn's view, as it resolves the legal problem without complete lapse of rights.

Key Terms
شيوع (shuyūʿ): Jointness; a right or ownership that is shared and undivided among co-owners.
عفو (ʿafw): Pardon; waiving the right to qisas by the victim's heir.
ربع الدية (rubʿ al-diyah): One-fourth of the blood money; the amount the pardoning owner must pay if he does not give half his share of the slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a jointly owned slave who kills both co-owners' fathers, what is the ruling according to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school?
A) The pardon by one co-owner makes everything void, including the other's right.
B) The pardoning owner must give half his share of the slave to the other owner or pay 1/4 of the diyat.
C) The non-pardoning owner can still demand qisas from the slave.
D) The slave becomes free.

Key Takeaway
In this intra-Hanafi dispute, the relied-upon position is that of the Sahibayn, which ensures the non-pardoning owner receives compensation, safeguarding the victim's right.

Diyat — Blood Money

Partial Diyat for Killing a Partially Owned Slave: The Hanafi Dispute
Ruling and proof for a master killing his partially owned slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position taken by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on the diyat obligation when a co-owner kills a jointly owned slave, and explain the legal reasoning that leads to qisas and diyah being dropped.

Core Idea
When a master kills his own partially owned slave, diyah and qisas are dropped because a master cannot be a debtor to his slave.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens when a master kills a slave he co-owns with another person? The matn indicates a ruling based on the principle that diyah belongs to the slain, and a master cannot owe a debt to his own slave. We will follow the reasoning of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two) and note the alternative narration attributed to Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and Core Issue
We have a case where Zayd, who is co-owner of a slave (owning half), kills that slave. What is his obligation? The answer depends on who owns the diyah.
2
State the Position of the Two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad)
According to the two, qisas and diyah are completely dropped. Instead, the master has an option: either give the co-owner (Bakr) ownership of half of his share (so Bakr gets 3/4 of the slave) or pay fidyah equal to one-fourth of the diyah (since the share is 1/4 of the slave).
This is from al-Ziyadat and al-Jami' al-Saghir.
3
Analyze the Proof (Dalil) for the Two's Position
The proof is that the wealth due as diyah is the right of the slain person (the slave). From this wealth, the slave's debts are paid and bequests executed. The heirs succeed him in this wealth after fulfilling his needs. However, a master cannot be a creditor to his own slave; therefore, the master has no claim to the diyah. Since the slain himself is not entitled to receive wealth from his slave (ownership blocks it), the heirs cannot succeed him either. Thus diyah is dropped.
This argument is attributed to the two in al-Ziyadat and to Abu Hanifa in al-Jami' al-Saghir.
4
Understand the Practical Difference (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
If we follow the two, the co-owner does not receive full diyah but gets compensated either by gaining ownership or receiving fidyah. If one held the opposite view (that diyah is not dropped), the co-owner might receive full diyah from the master.
5
Note the Authority Weight
This ruling is from the nawadir (rare transmissions) of al-Ziyadat and al-Jami' al-Saghir, not from the six core books. Therefore, its status is less established than zahir al-riwayah rulings.
The mufta bihi is not specified in the text.

Source Text

He was the owner of half a slave, so now he will become the owner of three-quarters of the slave. And if Zayd wishes, he may pay the ransom for half of his share, and the ransom will be one-fourth of the blood money. For this reason, according to Imam Abu Yusuf from the narration of al-Ziyadat, and according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) from the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir, Zayd will be obliged to do one of two things: either to make Bakr the owner of half of his share or to pay the ransom for that share. Since this share is 1/4 of the slave, the blood money will also be 1/4, i.e., two thousand five hundred dirhams. Proof of the two: 'And for them [the proof] is that what becomes due of wealth is the right of the slain because it is the substitute for his blood, and therefore his debts are paid from it and his bequests are executed from it. Then the heirs succeed him in it when his needs are fulfilled, and the master does not become entitled to a debt from his slave, so the heirs do not succeed him in it.' Translation: The proof of the two is that the wealth that becomes obligatory is the right of the slain because this wealth is the substitute for the slain's blood. Therefore, from this wealth the debts of the slain are paid and his bequests are executed. Then the heirs are the successors of the slain in this wealth after the fulfillment of his needs. And the master is not entitled to a debt from his slave, so the heirs will not succeed him in this wealth. Explanation: According to the narration of al-Ziyadat, this is the proof of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and according to the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir, this is the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa. The summary is that the wealth that becomes obligatory in blood money is in reality the right of the slain because it is the substitute and compensation for his blood. And this wealth is in reality the slain's. Its proof is that if the slain has a debt, it is paid from this wealth, and if he made a bequest, it is executed from this wealth. In any case, this is the wealth of the slain. Yes, if the slain has no need for it, then his rightful heirs become his successors. So when this is accepted as the right of the slain, the principle is that the master is not entitled to a debt from his slave. Therefore, here the slain himself is not entitled to receive any wealth from his slave. And when the slain himself is not entitled, the heirs cannot take this wealth as successors. Therefore, the two said that in the mentioned case, qisas and wealth (blood money) are completely dropped.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario where a master kills his slave, but only partially owns him. The ruling is that the diyah is proportional to the owner's share. However, there is a dispute within the Hanafi school: Abu Yusuf, based on one narration, says the owner has a choice to either give the other co-owner part of the slave or pay fidyah. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) agree on this choice. The proof provided is that the diyah belongs to the deceased slave, and since a master cannot be a creditor to his own slave, the diyah cannot be claimed by the master; thus qisas and blood money are both dropped. Instead, the master must compensate the co-owner.

Key Terms
فدیہ (fidyah): A ransom or compensation paid in lieu of blood money or other liability.
دیت (diyah): Blood money paid to the heirs of a victim of killing or injury.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment, i.e., execution for murder or bodily harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Qisas applies but diyah is reduced.
B) Both qisas and diyah are completely dropped.
C) The master pays full diyah and receives no compensation.
D) The master must pay diyah to the other co-owner.

Key Takeaway
When a master kills a co-owned slave, the diyah and qisas drop because the master cannot be a creditor to his slave; instead, the master must compensate the co-owner by giving ownership of half his share or paying fidyah.

Diyat — Blood Money

Blood Money for Killing a Slave: Capped Value or Full Price?
Ruling on diyah for accidental killing of a slave with dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two positions (capped vs. full value) for diyah of a slave and evaluate the opposing proof based on financial value analogy.

Core Idea
Slave compensation is capped at 9990 dirhams for a male; Abu Yusuf and Shafi'i demand full value based on maliyah.

When a slave is accidentally killed, should the killer pay the slave's full market value or a capped amount? In this passage, Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad set a maximum (9990 dirhams for a male, 4990 for a female), while Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i insist on the full value. The dispute turns on whether the compensation is for the blood or for the financial value (maliyah) of the slave. Let us examine the proof presented by the opposition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the exact ruling of Abu Hanifa & Muhammad (capped at 9990/4990) and of Abu Yusuf & al-Shafi'i (full value).
The cap is expressed as 'ten thousand minus ten' and 'five thousand minus ten'.
2
Understand the opponent's proof structure
Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i argue that compensation is a substitute for financial value (maliyah), not blood. They use two analogies: a sold slave killed before delivery, and usurpation (ghasb).
In both analogies, full value is paid by consensus.
3
Analyze the key premise
The master owns the slave only in terms of financial value, not humanity. Therefore, compensation must reflect that financial value fully.
This contrasts with free persons, where diyah is compensation for the person, not property value.
4
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a slave is worth 20,000 dirhams, Abu Yusuf and Shafi'i award 20,000; Abu Hanifa and Muhammad award only 9,990.
The cap severely limits compensation for high-value slaves.
5
Assess the completeness of the passage
The Hanafi response to the opponent's proof is missing in the source. Consider what a Hanafi rebuttal might look like—perhaps based on the slave's nature as property with a fixed value similar to diyah for a free person.
This lesson presents only one side of the argument; the full discussion would include the Hanafi counter-proof.

Section: Whoever kills a slave by mistake must pay his value, which shall not exceed ten thousand dirhams. If his value is ten thousand dirhams or more, judgment is given for ten thousand minus ten. And for a female slave, if her value exceeds the blood money of a free woman, [judgment is given for] five thousand minus ten. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i said: His value is due, whatever it may be. And if someone usurped a slave whose value is twenty thousand [dirhams] and he perished in his hand, his full value is due by consensus. Translation: A section on rulings concerning injury to a slave. Whoever kills a slave by mistake, then upon the killer is his value, which shall not exceed ten thousand dirhams. So if the slave's value is ten thousand dirhams or more, judgment is given for ten thousand dirhams minus ten. And for a female slave, if her value exceeds the blood money of a free woman, judgment is given for five thousand minus ten. This is according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i said: His value is due, whatever it may be. Explanation: Previously, rulings were given where injury was inflicted upon a slave. In this section, cases are discussed where injury is inflicted upon a slave. Therefore, it is said: If someone kills a slave by mistake, then instead of blood money, the slave's value is obligatory. But according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), the condition is that this value should not exceed the blood money of a free person. So if his value is, for example, ten thousand or more, then from the blood money, ten dirhams are reduced; it will be 9,990 dirhams. And that is all. And Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i say: The full value is obligatory, whatever it may be. And if someone usurped a slave whose value is, for example, twenty thousand, and the slave perished in the usurper's possession, then by consensus the full value is obligatory. Now listen to the proof of each. Proof of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i: 'For them [the proof is] that compensation is a substitute for financial value, and therefore it is obligatory for the master. And he does not own the slave except from the perspective of financial value. And if a sold slave is killed before delivery, the contract remains, and its existence is due to the existence of financial value, either as original or as substitute. And it becomes like [a slave] of little value and like usurpation.' Translation: The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i is that compensation is a substitute for financial value. For this reason, compensation is obligatory for the master, although the master owns the slave only in terms of financial value. And if a sold slave is killed before possession, the contract remains. The contract remains due to the continuation of financial value, either as the original or as a substitute. And it becomes like a low-value [slave] and like usurpation. Explanation: This is the proof of Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i. The summary is that compensation in such a case is a substitute for financial value, not a substitute for blood. And in the context of blood and life, a slave is not like a free person. And when compensation is determined to be a substitute for financial value, the full financial value must be given. Now, as for the question, what is the proof that compensation is a substitute for financial value? He said: The master's ownership of his slave is not by virtue of his humanity, otherwise the slave would be like a free person in terms of humanity. Rather, the master owns his slave in terms of financial value. And for this reason, in the case of killing a slave, compensation is given to the master. This is the proof that compensation is a substitute for financial value. Zayd bought a slave of Bakr. Zayd had not yet taken possession of the slave when Khalid killed this slave by mistake. Now the question is: does the contract of sale remain...
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This section discusses the diyah for accidentally killing a slave. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the killer must pay the slave's value but capped at 10,000 dirhams minus 10 dirhams (9,990 dirhams) for a male slave, and similarly for a female slave capped at 5,000 minus 10. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i argue that the full market value is due, with no cap. Their proof is that compensation in this case is for the financial value (maliyah) of the slave, not for blood. The master owns the slave only in terms of financial value, so the full value is owed. They support this by analogy with a sold slave killed before delivery (where the contract remains based on value) and with usurpation (ghasb), where full value is paid by consensus. The passage ends mid-sentence, with the Hanafi response not included.

Key Terms
قیمت (qimat): Market value or price of the slave.
دیت (diyah): Blood money for free persons; here used comparatively for slaves.
ضمان (daman): Liability or compensation for loss or damage.
مالیت (maliyyah): Financial value or monetary worth.
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation; wrongful taking of property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, what is the maximum amount payable for accidentally killing a male slave?
A) 10,000 dirhams exactly.
B) 9,990 dirhams.
C) The full market value with no cap.
D) 5,000 dirhams.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) caps slave compensation at 9,990 dirhams for a male, while Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i demand full value based on financial value reasoning.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
8 min
Diyah for a Slave: Humanity vs. Value (Abu Hanifa & Muhammad vs. Abu Yusuf)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on diyah for a slave: humanity vs. value

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi position on the diyah for a slave killed accidentally and explain the intra-madhhab difference with Abu Yusuf, including the proofs and the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A slave's diyah is based on humanity, not property: 9,990 dirhams for high-value slaves per Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

When a slave is accidentally killed, is the killer liable for the full market value of the slave or a fixed diyah amount? This question sparked a notable intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani on one side and Abu Yusuf on the other. The disagreement hinges on whether the slave's humanity or his property status should determine the blood money. In this lesson, we will walk through the arguments and see why the school ultimately adopted the view of the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa & Muhammad)
What is the mufta bihi ruling? For a high-value slave, the diyah is a fixed amount (9,990 dirhams); for a low-value slave, it is the slave's actual value. Identify the core principle: diyah is in exchange for humanity (آدمية), not property.
This position is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the relied-upon view.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Abu Yusuf holds that the diyah is the full market value of the slave, analogizing to usurpation (ghasb). Understand his two main proofs: (1) the ghasb analogy, (2) the contract of sale remains, so the buyer retains the right to full value.
The opposing view is also within the Hanafi school, so it is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine Abu Yusuf's dalil: he argues that just as usurpation (ghasb) requires full value, accidental killing of a slave should also require full value because the slave is property. Moreover, the sale contract remains after the killing (the buyer still has options), preserving the property aspect.
Abu Yusuf also cites the case of a low-value slave: if the diyah were based on humanity, why would the full value be paid there? He sees inconsistency.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rebut each of Abu Yusuf's proofs. For the ghasb analogy: usurpation only applies to property, not to a human with humanity. For the contract: the contract remains for the benefit of the buyer (option to take qisas or void), not for preserving property value. For low-value slaves: there is no fixed text, so by opinion (ra'y) the diyah is the slave's value; for high-value slaves, the reduction of 10 dirhams from the free diyah is based on the athar of Ibn Abbas.
The principle: when humanity and property cannot both be considered, humanity prevails.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Yusuf, the killer pays the full market price (e.g., 20,000 dirhams for a slave worth that). Under the mufta bihi view, the killer pays only 9,990 dirhams (or the slave's value if lower). Know which view to apply in fatwa.
This significant financial difference arises from the conceptual foundation of diyah.

Book of Diyat. Whether or not, the answer is that the wealth keeps the contract of sale remaining. A question arose: how can the contract of sale remain when the sale is not? Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah volume 15. The answer was given that for the continuation of the contract, wealth is needed. When the sold item exists, the original wealth remains; and if someone destroys the wealth, its substitute takes its place. Here, the substitute of the slave, i.e., the value that becomes obligatory on the killer, takes the place of the sold item (the slave). In any case, the monetary value remains, so the contract of sale also remains. In any case, here the continuation of the contract indicates that the guarantee is the substitute of the monetary value, so the full monetary value becomes obligatory on the killer. Then these people presented two evidences: 1. If the price of the killed slave is less than the diyah, why is the full value obligatory there? 2. If the slave was usurped, there also the full value is obligatory. Similarly, in this issue, full value will be obligatory. Two proofs of the two parties. And for Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the saying of Allah Almighty: 'and a diyah paid to his family' – He made it obligatory absolutely, and diyah is the name for the obligatory in exchange for humanity; and because in the slave there is the meaning of humanity such that he is obligated (for prayers etc.), and in him there is the meaning of property, and the humanity is the higher of the two, so it is obligatory to consider it by disregarding the lower when combination is impossible. Translation: And the proof of the two parties is the command of Allah Almighty: 'and a diyah paid to his family'. Allah Almighty made diyah absolutely obligatory, and diyah is the name for the obligatory that is obligatory in exchange for humanity; and because in the slave there are the meanings of humanity, and humanity is the higher of the two, so disregarding the lower (property) it is obligatory to consider humanity when combination between them is impossible. Explanation: The two parties presented two proofs. First, the mentioned verse in which Allah Almighty made diyah obligatory for accidental killing, and for killing a slave He did not command any other ruling, which indicates that for accidental killing absolutely this is the ruling, whether the killed is free or slave. Two aspects combine in a slave: one of humanity and the other of property. Because of the first, he is obligated for prayer, fasting, etc.; because of the second, he is owned. And among these two, humanity is strong and firm. Therefore, when combination of humanity and property becomes impossible, then humanity will be considered, and considering that, diyah becomes obligatory. Note: But there is a difference between free and slave, so we reduced ten dirhams from the diyah. Warning: Combining both is impossible; because considering humanity, diyah becomes obligatory, and considering property, value becomes obligatory, so only considering humanity, diyah was made obligatory. Page 292. Ashraf al-Bidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah volume 15. 291. Book of Diyat. Response to the proofs of the opposing party. 'And the guarantee of usurpation is in exchange for property, because usurpation only occurs upon property, and the continuation of the contract follows benefit, so that it remains after killing him intentionally, even though retaliation is not a substitute for property; thus is the matter of diyah. And in case of low value, what is obligatory is in exchange for humanity, but there is no text regarding it, so we estimated it with its value by opinion, unlike high value, because the value of a free person is estimated at ten thousand, and we reduced from it for the slave to show the lowering of his rank, and ten is specified by the effect of Abdullah ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both.' Translation: And the guarantee of usurpation is in exchange for property because usurpation is not removed except upon property, and the continuation of the contract follows benefit, even to the extent that after killing the slave intentionally the contract remains, even though retaliation is not a substitute for property; so similarly is the matter of diyah. And in low value, what is obligatory is in exchange for humanity, but there was no text regarding it, so we estimated it with its value by opinion, unlike high value, because the value of a free person is estimated at ten thousand, and we reduced from it for the slave to show the lowering of his rank, and ten is specified by the effect of Abdullah ibn Abbas. Explanation: From here the author responds to the proofs of the opposing party. You (Abu Yusuf) analogized to usurpation and made full value obligatory, but analogizing killing to usurpation is not correct, because usurpation is of property, so usurpation is considered as exchange for property, and full value becomes obligatory. Second, you said that the contract remains due to property; this is also wrong because if after the contract and before possession the slave of sale is killed intentionally, the contract will still remain even though retaliation is obligatory there, not property. It became known that the basis of the contract's continuation here is not on the continuation of property but on benefit, and that benefit is that if the contract remains, the buyer has the option: either to take retaliation from the killer or to cancel the sale. Summary: The basis of the contract's continuation is benefit, both in the case of intentional killing and in the case of accidental killing. So just as in intentional killing, due to benefit, the contract remains despite retaliation, similarly in accidental killing, in the case of obligation of diyah, due to benefit, the contract remains. Third, you analogized high value to low value; this is also wrong. Rather, we say that in the case of low value, the price is not a substitute for property but a substitute for humanity. But regarding how much diyah is obligatory, there was no text, so necessarily we used our opinion and made the diyah equal to its value. Now regarding high value, the reason we adopted the method is that the diyah and value of a free person in Sharia is ten thousand dirhams, but the rank of a slave is lower than free, so it became necessary to reduce something from the free person's diyah. Therefore we made it ten thousand dirhams (minus ten). Now the question remains why we reduced ten dirhams; the answer is that in the effect of Ibn Abbas, ten is specified. (Margin: Where is the slave's rank lower than free? We have explained this in detail in Dars al-Husami.)
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani on one side and Abu Yusuf on the other regarding the diyah (blood money) for a slave killed by mistake. The passage begins by presenting Abu Yusuf's argument: he analogizes killing a slave to usurpation (ghasb), where full value is due, and also argues that the contract of sale remains, thus the buyer's right to the value persists. Abu Yusuf also argues that if the slave's value is less than the diyah, why would full value be obligated? He then cites the example of usurpation. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad respond with two proofs. First, the Quranic verse (4:92) 'and a diyah paid to his family' is general for both free and slave. Second, they argue that in a slave there are two aspects: humanity and property. Humanity is higher, so when both cannot be combined, the higher (humanity) prevails, making diyah (blood money) obligatory rather than the full property value. However, they note a difference between a free person and a slave: a slave's rank is lower, so they reduce the diyah by ten dirhams from the free person's ten thousand dirhams, based on the athar of Abdullah ibn Abbas. For a low-value slave, since there is no fixed text, they set the diyah as the slave's actual value by opinion. The passage then refutes Abu Yusuf's specific arguments: (1) Usurpation is only for property, not for a human; (2) The contract remains for benefit (the option to take qisas or void the sale), not for preserving the property value; (3) The analogy of high-value to low-value is invalid because low-value has no text, so it is estimated by value, while high-value has a fixed reduced amount. The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money payable for accidental killing; in this passage, it is the fixed amount due for killing a slave, distinct from the full value.
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation or wrongful taking of property; used here as an analogy by Abu Yusuf to argue that full value is due for a slave killed accidentally.
قيمة (qimah): Market value or price; in this context, the value of the slave as property, which Abu Yusuf argues should be the diyah, but Abu Hanifa and Muhammad reject this for humanity-based diyah.
أثر (athar): A narration from a Companion (in this case, Abdullah ibn Abbas) that specifies the reduction of ten dirhams from the free diyah for a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, what is the diyah for a high-value slave killed accidentally?
A) The full market value of the slave
B) 10,000 dirhams (same as a free person)
C) 9,990 dirhams (10,000 minus 10 dirhams)
D) 10 dirhams

Key Takeaway
The diyah for a slave in the Hanafi school is based on his humanity, not his market value: for a high-value slave, it is 9,990 dirhams, and for a low-value slave, it is his actual value.

Diyat — Blood Money
