The Hanafi Rebuttal: Slave Diyat is Not Market Value
Rebutting opposing school's analogy of ghasp to qatl for slave diyat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi distinction between ghasp and qatl for determining slave diyat and evaluate the opposing school's analogy.

Core Idea
Slave diyat is capped by nass, not market value — ghasp analogy fails because qatl is about the person, not wealth.

This passage addresses a critical dispute in diyat law: should the blood money for a slave be his full market value? The opposing school analogizes to ghasp (usurpation) where full value is guaranteed. The Hanafi school rebuts this by distinguishing the nature of the obligation and invoking an athar of Ibn Abbas. Today, you will learn why this distinction matters and how it is derived.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opposing argument
The opposing school analogizes slave diyat to ghasp, requiring full market value. Understand their dalil: ghasp guarantees financial value, so qatl should too.
The opposing school likely includes the Shafi’i view.
2
State the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response: ghasp is about wealth, but qatl is about the person. The continuation of a contract after killing depends on benefit, not financial value. So the analogy fails.
See the commentary: 'ghasp is for wealth, qatl is for the person'.
3
Analyze the low-value vs high-value distinction
For a slave of low value, there is no nass, so qiyas is used and the full value is given. For high value, the nass (athar) caps it at 10,000 minus 5.
The text says 'qaleel al-qeemah' and 'kathir al-qeemah'.
4
Recognize the role of the athar
The specific number 9,995 comes from the athar of Abdullah ibn Abbas. This provides a clear textual basis for the cap.
The athar is cited as 'ta'ayyana al-asharah' (fixing at ten thousand minus five).
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: for a high-value slave (e.g., worth 15,000), Hanafi diyat is 9,995; opposing school would require 15,000.
This shows the consequence of accepting or rejecting the ghasp analogy.

Source Text

And the guarantee of usurpation is in exchange for financial value, because usurpation only pertains to wealth, and the continuation of the contract follows benefit, so it remains even after intentional killing, even though retaliation is not a substitute for financial value. Similarly is the matter of blood money. In the case of low value, what is obligatory is in exchange for humanity, but there is no text on it, so we determined it by its value through opinion, unlike high value because the value of a free person is fixed at ten thousand, and we reduced it in the case of a slave to show the degradation of his status, and fixing it at ten is based on the athar of Abdullah ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both). Translation: And the guarantee of usurpation is in exchange for financial value, because usurpation does not go away except on wealth. The continuation of the contract follows benefit, so even after intentional killing of a slave, the contract remains, even though retaliation is not a substitute for financial value. So similarly is the matter of blood money. In the case of low value, what is obligatory is in exchange for humanity, but there was no text on it, so we determined it by our opinion with its value. Unlike high value, because the value of a free person is fixed at ten thousand, and we reduced it for the slave to show the degradation of his status. And its fixing at ten is due to the athar of Abdullah ibn Abbas. Commentary: From here, the author responds to the arguments of the opposing school. They analogized to usurpation and made full value obligatory. But analogizing killing to usurpation is not correct because usurpation is about wealth, so the guarantee of usurpation is considered in exchange for financial value and full value is obligatory. And it was said that the contract remains due to financial value. This is also wrong because if after the sale, the slave is intentionally killed before delivery, the contract still remains even though retaliation is obligatory, not financial value. So the continuation of the contract depends on benefit, not on financial value. The benefit is that if the contract remains, the buyer has the option to take retaliation from the killer or to rescind the sale. So the continuation of the contract depends on benefit, both in case of intentional killing and accidental killing. So just as in intentional killing, the contract remains due to benefit despite retaliation, similarly in accidental killing, the contract remains due to benefit despite the obligation of blood money. And their analogy of high value to low value is also wrong. Rather we say that in the case of low value, the value is not in exchange for financial value but in exchange for humanity. But there was no text on how much blood money is obligatory, so they were compelled to use analogy and made its value obligatory. As for high value, the reason for our method is that the blood money and value of a free person in Shariah is ten thousand dirhams, but the status of a slave is lower than that of a free person, so it was necessary to reduce something from the free person's blood money, so we made it ten thousand. Why ten thousand? The answer is that in the athar of Ibn Abbas, ten is specified. The issue of where the slave's status is inferior to the free person's has been explained in detail in Dars al-Husami.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage is a rebuttal of the opposing school's argument that slave diyat should be analogized to ghasp (usurpation). The Hanafi position distinguishes ghasp from qatl: ghasp guarantees financial value because it pertains to wealth, while qatl is about the person. The author argues that the opposing school's analogy is flawed because the continuation of the contract after killing depends on benefit, not financial value. He also addresses the issue of low vs. high value: for low value, there is no nass, so qiyas is used; for high value, the nass of 10,000 for a free person is reduced for a slave to show status degradation, fixed at 10,000 minus 5 based on Ibn Abbas's athar.

Key Terms
ضمان الغصب (daman al-ghasb): Guarantee of liability for usurped property
دية (diyah): Blood money paid for unlawful killing or injury
أثر (athar): A saying or action of a Companion, here of Ibn Abbas

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects the ghasp analogy for slave diyat, fixing the cap at 9,995 based on nass and the lower status of the slave.

Diyat — Blood Money

Diyat for a Slave's Hand: Half Value Capped at 4995
Ruling on blood money for a slave's hand injury

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for diyat on a slave's hand and explain the qiyas to a free person's diyat, including the cap of 4995 dirhams.

Core Idea
A slave's hand diyat is half his value, capped at 4995, mirroring the free person's 5000 cap.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling for blood money when a slave's hand is cut. The ruling derives from analogy to a free person's hand, but with a cap that reflects the slave's lower status. Understanding this cap is crucial for correct compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is cutting a slave's hand. The ruling is that wajib blood money is half the slave's market value, but not exceeding 4995 dirhams.
The cap is expressed as 'five thousand except five', i.e., 5000 - 5 = 4995.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is qiyas (analogy) to the free person's hand. For a free person, half of the full diyat (5000 dirhams) is wajib.
The full diyat for a slave is capped at 9995, similar to the free person's 10000 minus 5.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The effective cause (illa) is that the hand is half of the human body. Thus, the ruling for the free person (half of full diyat) is transferred to the slave (half of full value), with the same reduction applied to show status degradation.
The reduction from half (e.g., 5000 to 4995) is applied consistently to maintain the slave's lower rank.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is a difference of opinion: some scholars may not accept the cap and require exactly half the value without reduction.
The Hanafi school relies on the established nass for the full value cap and applies the same logic to half.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa). The cap at 4995 is derived from the ruling for full value and is upheld in Zahir al-Riwayah.
This shows meticulous consistency in the Hanafi legal system.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وفي يد العبد نصف قيمته لا يزاد على خمسة آلاف إلا خمسة لأن اليد من الآدمى نصفه فتعتبر بكله وينقص هذا المقدار إظهار الانحطاط رتبته ترجمہ اہم قدوری نے فرمایا اور غلام کے ہاتھ میں اس کی قیمت کا نصف ہے جس کو پانچ ہزار سے پانچ کم دیا جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ آدمی کا ہاتھ اس کا نصف ہے تو اس کو کل پر قیاس کیا جائے گا اور یہ مقدار گھٹا دی جائے گی اس کے مرتبہ کی گراوٹ کو ظاہر کرنے کے لئے۔ تشریح ماقبل میں گذر چکا ہے کہ آدمی کے ہاتھ میں آدھی دیت واجب ہوتی ہے لہذا غلام کے ہاتھ میں آدھی قیمت واجب ہوگی اور اگر اس کی آدھی قیمت پانچ ہزار درہم سے زیادہ ہوتی ہے تو پانچ ہزار سے پانچ درہم کم واجب ہوں گے جس کی دلیل پہلے مسئلہ میں گذر چکی ہے یعنی کل کی صورت میں جو طریقہ اختیار کیا گیا ہے نصف کی صورت میں بھی وہی طریقہ اختیار کیا جائے گا۔
He (al-Quduri) said: And regarding the hand of a slave, half his value is due, not exceeding five thousand except five, because the hand of a human is half of him, so it is considered based on the whole, and this amount is reduced to show degradation of his status. Translation: Imam al-Quduri said: And in the hand of a slave, half of his value is due, which will be given as five thousand minus five. Because the hand of a human is half of him, so it is analogized to the whole, and this amount is reduced to show the degradation of his status. Commentary: It has passed earlier that in the hand of a free person, half of the full blood money is obligatory. Therefore, in the slave's hand, half of the value is obligatory. And if half of his value exceeds five thousand dirhams, then five thousand minus five dirhams will be obligatory, the proof of which has passed in the previous issue, i.e., the method adopted for the whole will also be adopted for the half.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for cutting a slave's hand: the diyat is half the slave's value, but it is capped at 4995 dirhams (5000 minus 5). The reasoning is based on analogy (qiyas) to the free person: just as a free person's hand injury incurs half the full diyat (5000 dirhams), a slave's hand injury incurs half the full value. However, because the full value for a slave is capped at 9995 (as per the previous lesson), half of that would be 4997.5, but the text says 'not exceeding 5000 except five,' which is interpreted as 5000-5=4995. This is to maintain consistency with the cap on full value and to show the slave's lower status.

Key Terms
يد (yad): Hand (in the context of injury)
نصف القيمة (nisf al-qimah): Half the market value of the slave

Key Takeaway

Diyat — Blood Money

Equivalence of Free Diyat and Slave Value Fractions
Establishing equivalence of free diyat and slave value for all injuries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that for any injury, the fraction of diyat due for a free person is equal to the same fraction of the slave's value.

Core Idea
Every fraction of free diyat maps to the same fraction of slave value — both are badal al-dam.

The Hanafi school establishes a fundamental equivalence between the diyat (blood money) for a free person and the value of a slave when compensating injuries. This principle derives from the concept that both are compensation for blood (badal al-dam). In this lesson, you will learn the rule, its basis, and how to apply it to specific injuries like the mawdihah wound.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
State the general rule: every fraction of diyat for a free person corresponds to the same fraction of value for a slave. This is the core teaching of the passage.
Memorize the Arabic phrasing: وَكُلُّ مَا يُقَدَّرُ مِنْ دِيَةِ الْحُرِّ فَهُوَ مُقَدَّرٌ مِنْ قِيمَةِ الْعَبْدِ
2
Understand the legal basis
Recognize that both diyat and slave value are considered badal al-dam (compensation for blood). This common illa justifies the analogy (qiyas) between the two.
The text says: الْقِيمَةُ فِي الْعَبْدِ كَالدِّيَةِ فِي الْحُرِّ إِذْ هُوَ بَدَلُ الدَّمِ
3
Apply to a specific injury
Work through the example of mawdihah (head wound exposing bone): for a free person, 1/20 of full diyat is due. Therefore, for a slave, 1/20 of his value is due.
This demonstrates that the rule applies to all fractional injuries, not just full diyat.
4
Distinguish from ghasp
Note the separate rule for usurpation (ghasp): if a slave dies in the usurper's possession, full value is due, not a fraction. This is because ghasp guarantee is a financial guarantee, not blood compensation.
The passage repeats: ضَمَانُ الْغَصْبِ ضَمَانُ الْمَالِيَّةِ

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكل ما يقدر من دية الحر فهو مقدر من قيمة العبد لأن القيمة فى العبد كالدية في الحر إذ هو بدل الدم على ما قررنا وإن غصب أمة قيمتها عشرون ألفا فماتت في يده فعليه تمام قيمتها لما بينا أن ضمان الغصب ضمان المالية ترجمہ اور ہر وہ جرم جس میں آزاد کی پوری دیت مقدر ہو لیس وہاں غلام کی پوری قیمت مقدر ہوگی۔ اس لئے کہ غلام کی قیمت آزاد کی دیت کے مثل ہے اس لئے کہ یہ (دیت اور قیمت دونوں ) خون کا بدل ہے جیسا کہ ہم ثابت کر چکے ہیں اور اگر کسی نے کوئی باندی ۔ غصب کی جس کی قیمت میں ہزار ہے پس وہ غاصب کے قبضہ میں مرگئی تو غاصب پر اس کی پوری قیمت واجب ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ ہے جو کہ ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں کہ غصب کا ضمان مالیت کا ضمان ہے۔ تشریح یعنی جہاں آزاد کی پوری دیت واجب ہوگی اور جہاں آزاد کی نصف دیت واجب ہوتی ہو، وہاں غلام میں نصف قیمت واجب ہوگی کیونکہ یہ دونوں دیت ہیں اور دونوں خون کا بدل ہیں’ودية مسلمة “ سے یہ بات واضح ہے لہذا اگر کسی آزاد کو ایسا زخم لگایا یعنی موضحہ جس میں دیت کا ۲۰/ اواجب ہے۔ وہاں غلام میں اس کی قیمت کا ۲۰/ اواجب ہو گا۔ اور ماقبل میں گذر چکا ہے کہ ضمان غصب مالیت کا ضمان ہے۔ لہذا کسی کی ایسی باندی غصب کی جس کی قیمت ہیں ہزار ہے اور وہ باندی ناصب کے پاس مرگئی تو غاصب پر پوری قیمت واجب ہوگی۔
And everything that is estimated from the diyat of a free person is estimated from the value of a slave, because the value for a slave is like the diyat for a free person, since it is compensation for blood, as we have established. And if someone usurps an amah (female slave) whose value is twenty thousand, and she dies in his hand, then the full value is due from him, because the guarantee of usurpation is a guarantee of financial value, as we have explained. Translation: And every crime for which the full diyat of a free person is fixed, there the full value of a slave will be fixed. Because the value of a slave is like the diyat of a free person, because both are compensation for blood, as we have proven. And if someone usurps a slave girl whose value is twenty thousand, and she dies in his possession, then the full value is due from him for the reason we have stated, that the guarantee of usurpation is a guarantee of financial value. Commentary: That is, wherever the full diyat of a free person is obligatory, and wherever half diyat of a free person is obligatory, there half value will be obligatory for a slave, because both are diyat and both are compensation for blood. This is clear from 'diyat muslimah?' So if a free person is wounded with a wound like mawdihah in which 1/20 of diyat is obligatory, then for a slave, 1/20 of his value will be obligatory. And it has passed earlier that the guarantee of usurpation is a guarantee of financial value. Therefore, if someone usurps a slave girl worth twenty thousand and she dies with the usurper, full value is due from the usurper.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage establishes a general principle: the diyat for a free person and the value for a slave are equivalent as 'badal al-dam' (compensation for blood). Therefore, whenever a specific fraction of the free diyat is due (e.g., full diyat, half diyat, or fractions for specific injuries), the same fraction of the slave's value is due. The example of a mawdihah (head wound exposing bone) is given: for a free person, 1/20 of diyat; for a slave, 1/20 of his value. The passage also reiterates the ghasp rule: if someone usurps a slave and she dies, full value is due because ghasp guarantee is financial.

Key Terms
بدل الدم (badal al-dam): Compensation for blood (i.e., life or injury)
دية (diyah): Blood money, financial compensation paid to the victim or heirs for homicide or bodily injury
قيمة العبد (qimat al-'abd): The market value of a slave at the time of injury

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 1/20 of the slave's value
B) Full slave value
C) Half slave value
D) 1/10 of slave value

Key Takeaway
The equivalence of free diyat and slave value for all injuries is a central Hanafi principle rooted in the concept of badal al-dam.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Qisas for Freed Slave After Injury
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qisas for freed slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on qisas for a freed slave who dies from a prior injury, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Qisas for a freed slave's death depends on whether the master is the sole heir — a key intra-Hanafi split.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: A slave's hand is cut, the master frees him, and then the slave dies from the injury. The question arises: is qisas (retaliation) applicable against the cutter? Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf condition qisas on the master being the sole heir, while Muhammad al-Shaybani denies qisas altogether, opting for monetary compensation. Understanding this split sharpens your ability to trace the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of different usul positions.

Guided Path
1
State the majority Hanafi position
Identify the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: qisas is executed if the only heir of the freed slave is the master; otherwise, no qisas.
This condition hinges on who inherits the right to qisas.
2
Identify the opposing view
State Muhammad al-Shaybani's position: no qisas in any scenario; only monetary compensation (arsh al-yad) is due.
Muhammad's ruling applies uniformly regardless of the master's role as heir.
3
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf, if the master is the sole heir, the cutter is executed; under Muhammad, the cutter pays compensation irrespective of heirs.
This difference affects whether the cutter loses life or pays money.
4
Analyze the underlying principle (inference)
Although the text does not provide explicit dalil, consider: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf likely view the master's right to qisas as inheritable, but only when no other heirs dilute that right. Muhammad likely sees the injury as occurring when the slave was property, so the master's subsequent freedom does not create a new right to qisas.
This step involves speculation; the full proof is not in the snippet.
5
Identify the mufta bihi (operative view)
Although not stated in the text, the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is typically followed in the Hanafi school, so the conditioned qisas position is likely mufta bihi.
Later sources confirm this as the relied-upon view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن قطع يد عبد فأعتقه المولى ثم مات من ذلك فإن كان له ورثة غير المولى فلا قصاص فيه وإلا اقتص منه وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف وقال محمد لاقصاص في ذلك وعلى القاطع أرش اليد وما
He said: And whoever cuts the hand of a slave, then the master frees him, and then he dies from that injury. If the slave has heirs other than the master, then there is no qisas in it; otherwise, qisas is executed from him (the cutter). This is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: There is no qisas in that, and the cutter owes the compensation (arsh) of the hand and...
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding qisas (retaliation) when a slave is injured, then freed, and then dies from the injury. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf distinguish: if the slave has heirs other than the former master (who is now free), then no qisas because the heirs are not the original owner; if the only heir is the master (who freed him), then qisas is executed because the master has the right. Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees: no qisas in either case; only monetary compensation (arsh) for the hand is due. The text is cut off, but likely continues with the reasoning.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment (eye for an eye) for intentional killing or injury.
أرش اليد (arsh al-yad): Compensation for the loss of a hand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only if the master is the sole heir
B) Always applied
C) Only if the slave has other heirs
D) Never applied

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, qisas for a freed slave's death is executed only if the master is the sole heir; otherwise, only arsh is due.

Diyah for a Slave's Hand: Cap and Analogy
Ruling on hand diyah of a slave with qiyas and a cap

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the diyah for a slave's hand, explain the 4,995 dirham cap, and derive the ruling through qiyas with the free person's hand diyah.

Core Idea
A slave's hand diyah is half his value but capped at 4,995 dirhams due to analogizing to the free person's half-diyah.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling on compensation for cutting off a slave's hand. The school uses a clear analogy: just as the hand is half the person, the diyah is half the full diyah. However, a subtle cap reflects the slave's subordinate legal status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is cutting off a slave's hand. The ruling: wajib diyah is half the slave's value, not exceeding 4,995 dirhams.
The exact wording: 'half his value, not exceeding five thousand except five.'
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is qiyas (analogy) based on the free person's hand diyah. The text states: 'because the hand of a person is half of him, so it is considered by the whole.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How the proof yields the ruling: For a free person, hand diyah is half the full diyah (5,000). By analogy, the slave's hand diyah is half his value (his 'full diyah').
The reduction of 5 dirhams is due to the slave's lower status (inhitat martabah).
4
Note the ikhtilaf (disagreement)
The passage does not mention other schools, but other madhahib may not apply the cap or may use a different basis for calculation.
Hanafi position is clear from Quduri's matn.
5
Evaluate the principle
The ruling is consistent with the part-whole logic: the diyah for any limb is proportional to the diyah of the whole person.
This establishes a framework for all diyah calculations for slaves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وفي يد العبد نصف قيمته لا يزاد على خمسة آلاف إلا خمسة لأن اليد من الآدمى نصفه فتعتبر بكله وينقص هذا المقدار إظهار الانحطاط رتبته
ترجمہ: اہم قدوری نے فرمایا اور غلام کے ہاتھ میں اس کی قیمت کا نصف ہے جس کو پانچ ہزار سے پانچ کم دیا جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ آدمی کا ہاتھ اس کا نصف ہے تو اس کو کل پر قیاس کیا جائے گا اور یہ مقدار گھٹا دی جائے گی اس کے مرتبہ کی گراوٹ کو ظاہر کرنے کے لئے۔ تشریح: ماقبل میں گذر چکا ہے کہ آدمی کے ہاتھ میں آدھی دیت واجب ہوتی ہے لہذا غلام کے ہاتھ میں آدھی قیمت واجب ہوگی اور اگر اس کی آدھی قیمت پانچ ہزار درہم سے زیادہ ہوتی ہے تو پانچ ہزار سے پانچ درہم کم واجب ہوں گے جس کی دلیل پہلے مسئلہ میں گذر چکی ہے یعنی کل کی صورت میں جو طریقہ اختیار کیا گیا ہے نصف کی صورت میں بھی وہی طریقہ اختیار کیا جائے گا۔
وكل ما يقدر من دية الحر فهو مقدر من قيمة العبد لأن القيمة فى العبد كالدية في الحر إذ هو بدل الدم على ما قررنا وإن غصب أمة قيمتها عشرون ألفا فماتت في يده فعليه تمام قيمتها لما بينا أن ضمان الغصب ضمان المالية
ترجمہ: اور ہر وہ جرم جس میں آزاد کی پوری دیت مقدر ہو لیس وہاں غلام کی پوری قیمت مقدر ہوگی۔ اس لئے کہ غلام کی قیمت آزاد کی دیت کے مثل ہے اس لئے کہ یہ (دیت اور قیمت دونوں) خون کا بدل ہے جیسا کہ ہم ثابت کر چکے ہیں اور اگر کسی نے کوئی باندی غصب کی جس کی قیمت بیس ہزار ہے پس وہ غاصب کے قبضہ میں مرگئی تو غاصب پر اس کی پوری قیمت واجب ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ ہے جو کہ ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں کہ غصب کا ضمان مالیت کا ضمان ہے۔ تشریح: یعنی جہاں آزاد کی پوری دیت واجب ہوگی اور جہاں آزاد کی نصف دیت واجب ہوتی ہو، وہاں غلام میں نصف قیمت واجب ہوگی کیونکہ یہ دونوں دیت ہیں اور دونوں خون کا بدل ہیں ’ودية مسلمة‘ سے یہ بات واضح ہے لہذا اگر کسی آزاد کو ایسا زخم لگایا یعنی موضحہ جس میں دیت کا ۲۰/۱ واجب ہے۔ وہاں غلام میں اس کی قیمت کا ۲۰/۱ واجب ہو گا۔ اور ماقبل میں گذر چکا ہے کہ ضمان غصب مالیت کا ضمان ہے۔ لہذا کسی کی ایسی باندی غصب کی جس کی قیمت بیس ہزار ہے اور وہ باندی غاصب کے پاس مرگئی تو غاصب پر پوری قیمت واجب ہوگی۔
He said: And for the hand of a slave, half his value, not exceeding five thousand except five, because the hand of a person is half of him, so it is considered by the whole, and this amount is reduced to show degradation in rank. Translation: Imam Quduri said: And for the hand of a slave, half his value, which will be given as five thousand minus five. Because the hand of a person is his half, so it is analogized to the whole, and this amount is reduced to show his degradation. Explanation: It passed earlier that for a free person's hand, half diyah is obligatory, so for a slave's hand, half value is obligatory. And if his half value exceeds five thousand dirhams, then five thousand minus five dirhams become obligatory, the reason for which passed in the previous issue, i.e., the method adopted for the whole will be adopted for the half. And everything that is quantified from the diyah of a free person is quantified from the value of the slave, because the value of the slave is like the diyah of the free person, as it is the blood-money on what we have established. And if someone usurped a slave-girl whose value is twenty thousand, and she died in his hand, then upon him is her full value, because we have explained that the guarantee of usurpation is a financial guarantee. Translation: And every injury for which the full diyah of a free person is quantified, there the full value of the slave is quantified. Because the value of the slave is like the diyah of the free person, because both are the blood-money. As we have proven, and if someone usurped a slave-girl whose value is twenty thousand, and she died in the hand of the usurper, then upon the usurper is her full value, for the reason we have stated that the guarantee of usurpation is the guarantee of financial value. Explanation: That is, where full diyah is obligatory for a free person, and where half diyah is obligatory for a free person, there half value is obligatory for a slave, because both are diyah and both are blood-money. It is clear from 'and diyah is established.' So if someone inflicted a wound (i.e., al-mudihah) on a free person for which 1/20th of diyah is obligatory, then for a slave, 1/20th of his value will be obligatory. And it passed earlier that the guarantee of usurpation is the guarantee of financial value. Therefore, if someone usurped a slave-girl whose value is twenty thousand, and she died with the usurper, then upon the usurper is full value.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the diyah for a slave's hand, followed by a general principle linking diyah for a free person to the value of a slave, and an example from ghasp (usurpation). The author begins by stating the ruling: the diyah for a slave's hand is half his value, but with a maximum limit of 5,000 dirhams minus 5 (i.e., 4,995 dirhams). This is because the hand is half of a person, so by analogy (qiyas) with a free person whose hand diyah is half of 10,000 dirhams (i.e., 5,000 dirhams), the slave's hand diyah is half his value. However, due to the slave's lower status (inhitat martabah), the amount is reduced by 5 dirhams. The commentary by Imam Quduri explains that if half the slave's value exceeds 5,000 dirhams, it is capped at 4,995 dirhams. The author then moves to a general rule: every quantifiable diyah for a free person (full or fraction) corresponds to the same fraction of the slave's value. This is because both diyah and value serve as blood money (badal al-dam). An example from ghasp is given: if a slave-girl worth 20,000 dirhams is usurped and dies in the usurper's possession, the usurper must pay her full value, as the guarantee for usurpation is based on financial value. This reinforces the principle that compensation for slaves is monetary, not the fixed diyah of free persons.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money or compensation paid for a homicide or injury.
عبد (abd): Slave, whose value is considered for compensation.
قطع يد (qat' yad): Cutting off a hand, a type of injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) 5,000 dirhams
C) 5,000 dirhams minus 5 dirhams
D) Full value of the slave

Key Takeaway
A slave's hand diyah is half his value but capped at 4,995 dirhams, derived by qiyas from the free person's half-diyah and reduced to reflect the slave's lower status.

Correspondence of Diyah and Value: General Rule and Ghasp Application
General rule of diyah-value correspondence and ghasp example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the general rule that any fraction of a free person's diyah corresponds to the same fraction of the slave's value, and identify the ghasp ruling that requires full value when a slave dies in usurpation.

Core Idea
Every fraction of diyah for a free person corresponds to the same fraction of a slave's value; ghasp of a slave requires full value as a financial guarantee.

This lesson extends the proportionality principle: for any injury, the compensation for a slave is the same fraction of his value as the diyah fraction for a free person. The passage then illustrates this with a ghasp case: if a slave-girl dies while usurped, the full value must be paid because usūlat (guarantee) is based on financial value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The passage states: 'Everything that is quantified from the diyah of a free person is quantified from the value of the slave.' This means any fractional diyah (full, half, 1/20th, etc.) for a free person corresponds to the same fraction of the slave's value.
The reason: value is to the slave as diyah is to the free person, since both are blood money (badal al-dam).
2
Apply the rule to an example
If a free person receives a wound (mudihah) that requires 1/20th of diyah, then for a slave, 1/20th of his value is wajib.
This confirms the proportionality across all fractions.
3
Examine the ghasp example
The author gives a second example: if someone usurps (ghasp) a slave-girl worth 20,000 dirhams and she dies in his possession, he must pay her full value.
4
Identify the basis for the ghasp ruling
The guarantee of usurpation (damān al-ghasp) is a financial guarantee, not a diyah guarantee. So full value is due, not a fractional amount.
This distinguishes ghasp from diyah cases.
5
Connect to the general rule
The ghasp example reinforces that compensation for slaves is based on value, but the nature of the claim (tort vs. property) determines whether it is fractional (diyah) or full (value).
The general rule applies only to injuries (jinayat), not to property usurpation.

As we have proven, and if someone usurped a slave-girl whose value is twenty thousand, and she died in the hand of the usurper, then upon the usurper is her full value, for the reason we have stated that the guarantee of usurpation is the guarantee of financial value. Explanation: That is, where full diyah is obligatory for a free person, and where half diyah is obligatory for a free person, there half value is obligatory for a slave, because both are diyah and both are blood-money. It is clear from 'and diyah is established.' So if someone inflicted a wound (i.e., al-mudihah) on a free person for which 1/20th of diyah is obligatory, then for a slave, 1/20th of his value will be obligatory. And it passed earlier that the guarantee of usurpation is the guarantee of financial value. Therefore, if someone usurped a slave-girl whose value is twenty thousand, and she died with the usurper, then upon the usurper is full value.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the diyah for a slave's hand, followed by a general principle linking diyah for a free person to the value of a slave, and an example from ghasp (usurpation). The author begins by stating the ruling: the diyah for a slave's hand is half his value, but with a maximum limit of 5,000 dirhams minus 5 (i.e., 4,995 dirhams). This is because the hand is half of a person, so by analogy (qiyas) with a free person whose hand diyah is half of 10,000 dirhams (i.e., 5,000 dirhams), the slave's hand diyah is half his value. However, due to the slave's lower status (inhitat martabah), the amount is reduced by 5 dirhams. The commentary by Imam Quduri explains that if half the slave's value exceeds 5,000 dirhams, it is capped at 4,995 dirhams. The author then moves to a general rule: every quantifiable diyah for a free person (full or fraction) corresponds to the same fraction of the slave's value. This is because both diyah and value serve as blood money (badal al-dam). An example from ghasp is given: if a slave-girl worth 20,000 dirhams is usurped and dies in the usurper's possession, the usurper must pay her full value, as the guarantee for usurpation is based on financial value. This reinforces the principle that compensation for slaves is monetary, not the fixed diyah of free persons.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasp): Usurpation; wrongfully taking and using another's property without permission.
ضمان المالية (daman al-maliyyah): Financial guarantee; liability to pay the market value of the property.
بدل الدم (badal al-dam): Compensation for blood; synonymous with diyah and, by extension, the value of a slave in injury cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a free person incurs an injury requiring 1/20th of diyah, what fraction of the slave's value is due for the same injury on a slave?
A) Full value
B) Half value
C) 1/20th of value
D) Fixed 500 dirhams

Key Takeaway
For injuries, slaves' compensation is proportional to their value mirroring free diyah fractions; for usurpation, full value is due as a financial guarantee.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Qisas for a Freed Slave's Death from a Prior Wound
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qisas for a freed slave's death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on qisas when a slave's wound causes death after manumission, and explain the reasoning (talil) behind the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
Qisas for a freed slave's death depends on who holds the right—master or heirs—causing an intra-Hanafi split.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario in qisas law: a slave's hand is cut, then the master frees him, and he dies from the wound. The Hanafi school is divided: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf distinguish based on the presence of other heirs, while Muhammad al-Shaybani denies qisas entirely. We will unpack the reasoning (talil) and practical consequences of this ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
State the two scenarios from the matn
Identify the two factual situations: (1) the slave has no heirs besides the master; (2) the slave has other heirs besides the master. Note the initial ruling given in the matn.
The matn first states the ruling conditionally: 'if he has heirs other than the master, no qisas; otherwise qisas is taken.'
2
Identify the ruling of the two Shaykhs in each scenario
Attributed to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: in scenario (1) qisas is obligatory; in scenario (2) no qisas. Only monetary compensation (arsh and loss) is due.
This is the position presented as the standard in the text.
3
Identify Muhammad's ruling in each scenario
Imam Muhammad holds that in neither scenario is qisas applicable. His view: only arsh for the hand and compensation for the loss from injury until manumission are due.
Muhammad consistently denies qisas because the initial injury was against a slave (property), so only financial remedies apply.
4
Analyze the talil (reasoning) behind the dispute
The key legal concept is that qisas becomes obligatory at death but is linked back to the time of injury. At injury, the right to seek remedy belongs to the master (as owner of the slave). At death, the right belongs to the heirs. If the master is the sole heir, the right-holder is the same, so qisas is enforceable. If there are other heirs, the right-holder is ambiguous, so qisas is dropped. Muhammad argues that the injury occurred while the victim was property, so no personal right to qisas ever arose.
The term 'ishtibah' (ambiguity) is central: when the right-holder is unclear, qisas cannot be executed.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and the thamarah al-khilaf
The text presents the view of the two Shaykhs as the relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah). The practical difference: if the master is the sole heir, under the majority view the cutter is executed; under Muhammad's view, he only pays arsh and compensation.
In the Hanafi school, the agreement of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is preferred, so the mufta bihi is that qisas applies when the master is the sole heir.

وإنما لم يجب القصاص فى الوجه الأول لاشتباه من له الحق لأن القصاص يجب عند الموت مستند إلى وقت الجرح فعلى اعتبار حالة الجرح يكون الحق للمولى وعلى اعتبار الحالة الثانية يكون للورثة فتحقق الاشتباه وتعذر الاستيفاء فلايجب على وجه يستوفي وفيه الكلام
ترجمہ: اور پہلی صورت میں قصاص واجب نہ ہوگا، من له الحق، کے مشتبہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اس لئے کہ قصاص موت کے وقت وقت جرح کی جانب مستند ہو کر واجب ہوتا ہے۔ حالت جرح کے اعتبار سے حق آقا کا ہوتا ہے اور حالتِ ثانیہ کے اعتبار ورثا کا حق ہوتا ہے تو اشتباہ متحقق ہو گیا اور قصاص کی وصولیابی متعذر ہوگئی تو اس طریقہ پر واجب نہ ہو سکا جس کو وصول کر لیا جائے اور اس وجوب میں
تشریح: جو صورت اتفاقی ہے قصاص واجب نہ ہونے کی یہ اس کی دلیل ہے یعنی جب کہ آقا کے علاوہ بھی اس کا کوئی وارث ہو تو یہاں قصاص واجب نہیں ہے۔ کیوں؟ اس لئے من له الحق مشتبہ ہے قصاص وصول کرنے کا حق کس کو ہے اگر وقت جرح کا اعتبار کیا جائے تو حق آقا کو ہے اور اگر وقتِ موت کا لحاظ کیا جائے تو حق وارث کو ہے جب من له الحق میں شبہ ہو گیا تو شبہ کی وجہ سے قصاص کو ساقط کرنا پڑا۔ فلايجب على وجه .... الخ - یعنی اگر چہ قاطع کا فعل بذات خود یہاں موجب قصاص ہے اس لئے نفس وجوب قصاص ثابت
He said: And whoever cut off the hand of a slave, then the master freed him, then he died from that, so if he has heirs other than the master, there is no qisas in it, otherwise qisas is taken from him. And this is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: There is no qisas in that, and upon the cutter is the arsh of the hand and what was lost of it from that until he freed him, and the excess is void. Translation: Muhammad said: And whoever cut off the hand of a slave, then the master freed him, then that slave died from that cutting of the hand, so if besides the master he has heirs, then there is no qisas in it, otherwise qisas will be taken from him. And this is the statement of the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). And Muhammad said: There is no qisas in it, and upon the cutter is the arsh of the hand and the loss that occurred in it until the time of manumission, and the excess is void. Explanation: The scenario is: Khalid has a slave Zayd; Bakr cut off Zayd's hand, and after the amputation Khalid freed Zayd, then after freedom Zayd died from the spread of that wound. What is the ruling on Bakr? There are two scenarios: (1) The deceased Zayd has no heir other than the master—no one from the Quranic heirs or agnatic relatives, only the manumitter (mu'tiq) is his heir. (2) There is some other heir besides the master. In the second scenario, by agreement, qisas is not obligatory; rather, the arsh of the hand and the loss caused by the cut before manumission are obligatory. However, in the first scenario there is disagreement: according to Imam Muhammad, here too qisas is not obligatory, but rather the same arsh and loss are obligatory; according to the two Shaykhs, in this scenario qisas is obligatory. In other words, according to Imam Muhammad, in no scenario is qisas obligatory, while according to the two Shaykhs, in the first scenario qisas applies, and in the second it does not. And qisas is not obligatory in the first scenario due to ambiguity of the right-holder, because qisas becomes obligatory at the time of death but is linked back to the time of injury. Considering the state of injury, the right belongs to the master; considering the second state (death), the right belongs to the heirs. Thus ambiguity is realized and execution becomes impossible, so qisas cannot be obligatory in a way that can be executed. And in that obligation... Explanation: The case where by agreement qisas is not obligatory—this is its proof: When besides the master there is some heir, qisas is not obligatory. Why? Because the right-holder (man lahu al-haqq) is ambiguous: if we consider the time of injury, the right belongs to the master; if we consider the time of death, the right belongs to the heir. When the right-holder becomes ambiguous, qisas must be dropped. 'So it is not obligatory in a way...' i.e., even though the cutter's act itself is grounds for qisas, so the essence of qisas is established.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding qisas for the death of a slave whose hand was cut off, then freed, and then dies from the wound. The base matn states the ruling: if the slave has heirs other than the master, no qisas; otherwise, qisas is imposed. This is attributed to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two Shaykhs). Imam Muhammad holds that in neither case is qisas applicable; instead, the cutter must pay arsh (compensation) for the hand and compensation for the loss in value from the time of injury until manumission, with any excess (the value of the hand after manumission) being void. The commentary explains two scenarios: (1) the master is the sole heir, and (2) other heirs exist. In the second scenario, all agree no qisas. In the first, the two Shaykhs say qisas, while Muhammad says only monetary compensation. The reasoning given is that qisas must be executed based on the right-holder. At the time of the injury, the master (as owner) has the right to qisas (since the slave was property, but the injury is against property? Actually, qisas for murder is a personal right, but here the slave's death became that of a free person after manumission. The right to qisas for a free person belongs to the heirs. At the injury, the master had a right to compensation (property), but after death, the heirs have the right to qisas. In scenario 1, the master becomes the sole heir, so the same person holds both rights, allowing qisas. In scenario 2, the right is split, causing ambiguity, so qisas is dropped. Muhammad consistently denies qisas because the initial injury was when the slave was property, so only financial compensation is due.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation, specifically capital punishment for causing death.
أرش (arsh): Fixed compensation for a specific injury, here the hand.
سراية الجرح (sirayat al-jarh): The spread of the wound leading to death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does qisas not apply when the freed slave has other heirs besides the master?
A) Because the slave was once a slave and thus cannot have qisas
B) Because the right-holder becomes ambiguous between the master and other heirs
C) Because the master waived his right by freeing the slave
D) Because the wound was not the direct cause of death

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi qisas, when a slave's wound leads to death after manumission, the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) rule that qisas applies only if the master is the sole heir; otherwise financial compensation is due, while Imam Muhammad denies qisas in all cases.

Diyat — Blood Money

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Does Emancipation Cut Off Qiṣāṣ in Intentional Injury?
Response of the two shaykhs to Imam Muhammad's argument

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that emancipation does not cut off qiṣāṣ in intentional injury, and evaluate Imam Muhammad's opposing analogy.

Core Idea
Emancipation only cuts off extension in accidental injuries due to confusion; in intentional, no confusion, so qiṣāṣ remains.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of emancipation (itq) on the right to qiṣāṣ when a master wounds his own slave and then frees him before death. Imam Muhammad argued that emancipation cuts off qiṣāṣ by analogy to accidental cases where it cuts off arsh. The two shaykhs, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, responded with a nuanced distinction based on the nature of the right and the absence of confusion about who holds it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
What is the specific scenario? A master intentionally wounds his slave, then emancipates him, and the slave dies from the injury. Does the emancipation cut off the right to qiṣāṣ?
2
State Imam Muhammad's position and his analogy
Imam Muhammad argues that emancipation cuts off qiṣāṣ in all cases, analogizing to accidental injury where emancipation cuts off arsh. He relies on the principle that difference in cause is considered when it affects the ruling.
His argument: just as ownership by marriage vs. right hand affects permissibility, ownership at injury vs. at death should affect qiṣāṣ.
3
Analyze the two shaykhs' response
The two shaykhs reject the analogy. They explain that emancipation cuts off extension (sirāyah) only in accidental injury because of confusion (ishtibāh) about who holds the right. In intentional injury, no confusion arises.
The key distinction is the nature of the right: qiṣāṣ (fixed penalty) vs. arsh (financial compensation).
4
Examine the concept of confusion (ishtibāh)
In accidental injury, the entitlement to arsh shifts from master (at injury, slave owned) to slave's heirs (at death, slave free), causing confusion. In intentional, qiṣāṣ is always received by the master: originally as owner, or by vicegerency after emancipation. Thus no confusion.
The slave is deemed free for qiṣāṣ but has no heir other than the master, so the master undertakes it.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? According to the two shaykhs, qiṣāṣ remains wajib and the master may be executed if he did not consent. According to Imam Muhammad, the right is cut off.
The mufta bihi position is the two shaykhs' view.

Source Text

شیخین کی طرف سے امام محمد کے مستدلات کا جواب
والإعتاق لا يقطع السراية لذاته بل لاشتباه من له الحق وذلك فى الخطأ دون العمد لأن العبد لا يصلح مالكا للمال فعلى اعتبار حالة الجرح يكون الحق للمولى وعلى اعتبار حالة الموت يكون للميت لحريته فیقضى منه ديونه وينفذ وصاياه فجاء الاشتباه أما العمد فموجبه القصاص والعبد مبقى على أصل الحرية فيه وعلى اعتبار أن يكون الحق له فالمولى هو الذى يتولاه إذ لا وارث له سواه فلا اشتباه في من له الحق
ترجمہ اور اعتاق بذات خود سرایت کو ختم کر دینے والا نہیں ہے بلکہ، من له الحق کے اشتباہ کی وجہ سے (اعتاق قاطع سرایت ہے) اور یہ اشتباہ خطاء میں ہوتا ہے نہ کہ عمد میں اس لئے کہ غلام مال کا مالک بنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا تو حالت جرح کے اعتبار کرنے میں حق آقا کا ہوتا ہے۔ اور حالت موت کا اعتبار کرنے میں میت کا حق ہوتا ہے اس کے آزاد ہونے کی وجہ سے پس اس سے اس کے قرضے ادا کئے جائیں گے اور اس کی وصیتیں نافذ کی جائیں گی تو اشتباہ پیدا ہو گیا بہر حال عمد پس اس کا موجب قصاص ہے اور غلام قصاص میں اصل حریت پر باقی ہے اور اس اعتبار سے بھی کہ حق غلام کا حق ہے پس آقا ہی تو (خلافت کے طریقہ پر) اس کا متولی ہوتا ہے اس لئے کہ آقا کے علاوہ اس کا کوئی وارث نہیں ہے تو من له الحق میں کوئی اشتباہ نہیں ہے۔ تشریح شیخین کی طرف سے امام محمد کے مستدلات کا جواب دیا جا رہا ہے یہ ان کے اس استدلال کا جواب ہے جو فر مایا تھا کہ اعتقاق قاطع سرایت ہے تو جواب دیا ہاں اعتاق قاطع سرایت ہے لیکن قتل خطاء میں نہ کہ عمد میں اور ہماری گفتگو عمد میں ہورہی ہے نہ کہ قتل خطاء میں۔ سوال... اس کی کیا دلیل ہے اعتاق خطاء میں قاطع سرایت ہے عمد میں نہیں ہے؟ جواب اس لئے کہ اعتاق کو جہاں قاطع سرایت قرار دیا گیا ہے وہ اس لئے تا کہ اشتباه من له الحق لازم نہ آئے اور یہ صرف خطاء کے لئے مخصوص ہے نہ کہ عمد میں کیونکہ موجب عمد تو قصاص ہے اول حالت کے اعتبار سے اس کو حق آقا قرار دیا جائے یا آخر وقت کے اعتبار سے اس کو حق غلام قرار دیا جائے دونوں صورتوں میں قصاص کو وصول کرنے والا آقا ہو گا۔ اول میں اصالۃ اور ثانی میں خلافة، بہر حال من له الحق میں کوئی اشتباہ نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے قصاص واجب ہوگا۔ البتہ خطا کی صورت میں یہ اشتباہ ہوسکتا تھا کہ اول کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے ارش کا مالک آقا ہوگا کیونکہ اس وقت وہ غلام تھا جو مال کا مالک بننے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا اور ثانی صورت میں ارش کا مستحق خود غلام ہوگا کیونکہ وہ اس وقت آزاد ہے لہذا اس کا یہ مال اس کے ورثا کے درمیان تقسیم ہو اور اس مال سے اس کے قرضے ادا کئے جائیں اور اس مال میں اس کی وصیتیں نافذ ہوں۔ بہر حال اشتباہ خطا میں تھا اس لئے خطا میں اعتاق کو قاطع سرایت قرار دیا گیا ہے عمد میں نہیں۔
Commentary: This is the proof of estimation. There is no doubt in it, rather certainty, that the master's authority is established in both cases, i.e., the one for whom the right is apportioned (the master) is known, and the ruling of qiṣāṣ is unified, so inevitably one must hold the obligation of qiṣāṣ and the obligation of its collection. As for the first case, the one for whom the right is apportioned is unknown, so analogizing it to this is not correct. 2. And what did you say, O Imam Muhammad, that difference of cause is like the level of the entitled? This is not a principle; rather, where difference of cause does not result in difference in ruling, difference of cause is like non-existent and disregarded. As for the case you presented, there difference of cause is considered due to difference in ruling, because ownership by marriage and ownership by right hand differ, since in the first, permissibility (of marriage) is intended, and in the second, ownership is intended, and permissibility is subsidiary and subordinate. In any case, Imam Muhammad's inference from this particular and this principle is not correct. Response from the two shaykhs to Imam Muhammad's proofs: And emancipation does not cut off the extension (sirāyah) by itself, but due to confusion regarding who holds the right, and that is in accidental (killing) not intentional, because a slave is not capable of owning property. Considering the state of injury, the right belongs to the master; considering the state of death, it belongs to the deceased due to his freedom, so from it his debts are paid and his bequests executed, thus confusion arises. As for intentional, its consequence is qiṣāṣ, and the slave remains upon the original (principle of) freedom regarding it, and considering that the right is his, the master is the one who undertakes it (by way of vicegerency), for he has no heir besides him, so there is no confusion regarding who holds the right. Translation: And emancipation does not in itself terminate the right, but due to confusion of who holds the right (emancipation is a cutter of extension), and this confusion occurs in accidental (injury) not in intentional, because a slave is not capable of owning property. So considering the state of injury, the right belongs to the master; considering the state of death, the right belongs to the deceased due to his freedom, so from it his debts are paid and his bequests executed, thus confusion arises. As for intentional, its consequence is qiṣāṣ, and the slave remains upon the original (principle of) freedom regarding it, and from the perspective that the right is the slave's right, the master is the one who undertakes it (by way of vicegerency), for he has no heir besides him, so there is no confusion regarding who holds the right. Commentary: The response from the two shaykhs to Imam Muhammad's proofs is being given. This is the answer to his inference that emancipation cuts off extension. So they answered: Yes, emancipation cuts off extension, but in accidental killing, not in intentional, and our discussion is about intentional, not about accidental killing. Question: What is its proof that emancipation cuts off extension in accidental and not in intentional? Answer: Because where emancipation is considered a cutter of extension, it is to avoid necessity of confusion regarding who holds the right, and this is specific to accidental, not intentional, because the consequence of intentional is qiṣāṣ. Whether one considers the right to belong to the master based on the initial state or to the slave based on the final time, in both cases the one receiving qiṣāṣ is the master: in the first by way of original right, and in the second by vicegerency. In any case, there is no confusion regarding who holds the right. Therefore, qiṣāṣ is obligatory. However, in accidental, this confusion could occur: considering the first, the owner of the arsh would be the master because at that time the slave was not capable of owning property; in the second case, the slave himself would be entitled to the arsh because he is free at that time, so this wealth is distributed among his heirs, and his debts are paid from it, and his bequests are executed from it. In any case, the confusion was in accidental, so in accidental emancipation is regarded as a cutter of extension, not in intentional.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). The issue: does emancipation (itq) cut off the right to qiṣāṣ when the master injures his own slave? Imam Muhammad argued that it does, analogizing to accidental cases where emancipation cuts off arsh. The two shaykhs respond that emancipation only cuts off extension (sirāyah) in accidental injuries because of confusion about who holds the right (the master or the freed slave), but in intentional injuries, the consequence is qiṣāṣ, and there is no confusion: whether we consider the time of injury (slave owned by master) or the time of death (slave free), the master is always the one to receive the diyah or execute qiṣāṣ. In intentional, the slave is deemed free for qiṣāṣ, but since he has no heir, the master acts as deputy. Thus qiṣāṣ is established. The passage first refutes a previous argument by Imam Muhammad regarding the principle of difference of cause, then provides the substantive response with a question-and-answer format to clarify.

Key Terms
اعتاق (ītāq): Emancipation of a slave; setting free.
سرایت (sirāyah): Extension of the right/duty; here, the continuation of the right to qiṣāṣ or diyah from the time of injury to death.
من له الحق (man lahu al-ḥaqq): The one who holds the right; the person entitled to qiṣāṣ or diyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), why does emancipation not cut off the right to qiṣāṣ in intentional injury?
A) Because the slave is not free at the time of injury
B) Because confusion about who holds the right does not arise in intentional injury
C) Because qiṣāṣ can only be exacted if the victim is free
D) Because the master retains ownership until death

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, emancipation cuts off the right to arsh in accidental injury due to confusion, but does not cut off the right to qiṣāṣ in intentional injury because no confusion arises.
